O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, very dear children, I have finished this book which is the end of the science of medicine assembled from its employment, and I have completed it by its exposures and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw in vision that I must complete this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the little descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have performed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arises the error and the vanity, and the closures of the understanding and the displacement of the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I must bring it to life together the ordination of this practitioner according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will join together the forms of the instruments of cautery and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary. And because no wise man of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he must know who comes into this subject thoroughly the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he can discern the judgments of the limbs, and the forms and the joints and the separations of them, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and arteries and the number of seeds, and the movement of semen and its rest.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates taught us that with the hand we must not be lazy, but must work diligently; and the same in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We must say at the outset of this book that whoever is not learned in the things that are before him, if he is arrogant and does not humble himself; as I have often seen happen, many people ruin themselves through these very things that are related to this science and abandon both science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who copped his testicles with a pincer, or pulled out the hair of a woman; and he bled so much that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another marvel which treats a stone of a bladder, and the stone was great; if it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in the hon for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already heard of it being called to treat, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and indeed if it were cut out it would surely die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another marvel which treats a limb broken in our land, and with the bruise caused by the wound; and the physicians of this land do not know how to treat the bruise upon the wound as these stars are held together by strong ligature, and do not allow the wound to bleed at all, and leave it thus until it is finished; and they command that it not be moved, and that the limb be entirely freed and the bone and marrow be lost forever.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I come to him and hasten to loosen the limb; and when I find it dislocated, it is without pain and without feeling any discomfort.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in every way the corruption has already been confirmed or the limb has become deformed, and it cannot be healed; and the corruption continues to grow as long as the limb remains whole and intact.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus too with other matters which undermine the body, such as tumors, boils, and inflammation caused by the malice of its master.</start_of_turn
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound caused by a melancholic tumor, it is only useful to touch it with fire if it is not in some part already corrupted to such an extent that everything corrupted must be removed.</start_of_turn
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, take heed, for the work of the hands has become divided into twelve parts: that is to say, there is peril in many things. I will show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For you must take care that your limbs remain whole, so that no evil word can be spoken of you. If you take your weapons in custody and begin your ailments lightly and firmly, and use the best way, then by the grace of God you will come to health and be well; and let the curable diseases depart from your heart with peace. Stay away from those things that make you doubt, and trust in your arms that you may go from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The alien whispers in the ears of his attendants: "Do not take me for a madman who is mad about nothing; for I am not remembered as a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and surgical cautery with water-based medicine, and this chapter orders from the head down; forms of instruments, and instruments for cautery, and everything necessary for the work
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with fracture and piercing, and of abscesses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter orders and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and strains, and similar matters; and it is ordered from the head downwards, and from the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So, as we have recalled from the work, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the aid and the danger of neglecting complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the danger, is the longest word and the most subtle science and the secret response; and concerning this, many speak, and they agree with this; and I find that their words are insufficient, because I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or when there is matter, for since there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion that is warm in sense of matter, and a complexion that is dry in sense of matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For in complexion hot and dry mixed with matter, some say it brings no relief and declare that cautery is of great aid; others say the opposite: that cautery is of no value in disease except when it comes from heat and dryness.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture with the complexion of the fire, you find the body dry.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, there is no fire that does not yield to me more than that which has been proved by experience, and which knows by long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of humoral conditions, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the issues and the space of their tensions; of other humors we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the others yield to the cautery and agree with it.</start_of_turn
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, children, that fire cautery is more effective for certain ailments than burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and brings no further pain than to the limb that is being treated, and harms no other part besides that.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medical preparations come from one member to another by mixing, and cause diseases in the limb with great health; and by chance it often happens that the patient feels unwell. The fire of life for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not make me do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know ye, son, that it is necessary to agree in what tense the cauteries should be made, and their precautions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is permissible in all tenses, for the harmful effects that are coming from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and besides, if the cauteries are for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait for a greater harm to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, my son, that because fools do, it follows that the malady which is cured by cautery has no remedy; for he says it is so. But he lies, for cautery is nothing but medicine which moves the complexion and dries humors which are the cause of pain, and is more useful than medicine for hastening its value and for the virtue of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And know that no disease ever departs according to the complexion of the patient and the course of the disease and its virtue; and are gathered in it the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if these are not administered with cautery when there is little superfluity and moisture, for indeed cautery is better for pain than meats and similar things, and part of the pain does not return again; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that because cautery is called behind medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery is better than medicine, but their understanding is false, for indeed cautery is behind medicine because whenever we administer other treatments for any disease and they do not help, then we administer the cautery, and it is better.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, although cautery is behind medicine, it is not according to the intentions of fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that gold cautery is duller than iron, and they say that fire is only useful for the quality of the gold and for its fineness; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and I have found that it is seen in some men; and gold cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, when you burn the instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is tarnished by the color of gold, and when it is so cold; and if you burn it too much; if there is too much fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have learned it in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from head to toe, for this reason that the way should be easier to find.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive oil cauteries are useful for moisture and cold, for there are many diseases caused by a condition called "soda," and by the abundance of humors that descend from the head as sweat, and in the ears, and for many other complaints such as toothache, earache, and neck and throat pain, and even for many diseases that arise from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged by means of a soluble medicine which modifies the head of the joint, two or three times, according to what the physician deems useful and agreeable to the patient's custom; and then repeat the head of the joint of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then he makes him sit between your hands, and put his hands down on his feet; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his thumb between his two nails; and there or will come your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the base then withdraw the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and make descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then withdraw your hand slightly, and renew the cautery until you see the bone somewhat; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that take one moment of balsam, and put in awe and soak a cotton pad inside, and take out the bone, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft bandage. And leave it on until the scab has become bony; after that cure the wound of the burn which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the ancients, that the more time passes over a wound, the more it purges; and for this reason they aid the wound with movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that none of these men say that we must leave the cautery on for so long that part of the bone is burnt, and then we must renew what is burnt on the bone, and it must be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that we must leave the cautery on for so long as a woman puts in her girdle for that the humors issue out loosely; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; and then we must cure and dress it.</start_of_turn>
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good for all things, for in some men or if there is fear of pain; and I think that I ought to leave it; for the head of the shoulder is easily loosened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and even when the pain is slight by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more salve and merciful for me, and for this reason I do this thing in this manner.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, the patient must use herbs, pills which are called «cochie», and vomiting of the head, oils and poultices; and if we make the cautery as we have said before, it is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that if the patient’s condition is strong and not too weak; then the cautery must be performed as we have said above.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After the cautery is done on the bone of the head as we have said, and you have done the cautery of the vein which is called the «vasselz»; and that is where you put the sponges; hold your hand so that you do not see blood until the bone: the patient feels more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of that later; and it is recommended that the cautery of the horns be more subtle than that of the middle of the head, and that is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Dou cautere dou chief,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When in a part of the shoulder comes sudden pain, and the disease is extended up to the armpit, and the limb is expelled by medicines that are modified, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases; and all this has not profited: therefore you must make cauteries in two ways, that is to say of medicine and fire.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of inflammation while he is still sane; and if you see that he does not recover from this with any of the medicines I have written or if you wish to treat him with other medicines that are not mentioned.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is as follows in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is as follows in this manner.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a loop or it has a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and put out the painful limb, and hold your hand and touch the burn with a slight movement until half of the thickness of the hair is burned; and keep your hand still so that the artery does not burn, that is to say that it is blistered, and drain abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After having put on cotton wool around the limb, take it out after two or three days. Then put on moist cotton wool in the burrow and cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb, take it out after two or three days. Then put on moist cotton wool in the burrow and cure the limb of swelling until it is healed. Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cauterize an abscess as we have previously said in the chapter on diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that it does not suffice with just the cautery, then you must abstain from the cautery which is called "cultellare" while it is still green; and if you must remove the limb leaving a mark of half an inch long, and you move your hand once, and strain so that you do not cover the artery and do not feel pain; and be wary of the jaw that bites when you move it, and that it does not cause more damage than the pain and spasm, and be wary of the evacuation of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting causes great fear and discomfort to those who do not know how to handle it, and who are not experienced and learned; and leave the work in peace; but I will tell you how to staunch blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you notice that the former cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the other side as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the previous and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	If you notice that the former cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the other side as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of scissors; and this cautery is better than the previous and more helpful.

de la torture de la bouche	After pricking all around the painful ear, or around the joint, if the pain persists in both places, then loosen a little from the root of the ear until you have marked the length; and take ten points around the ear; then cure the length as soon as it is healed.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those that move from moisture, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery that resembles that which comes from drying and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this semblance of torture that is made of fumes of hydras and purges of head and gargling, know that it is worth nothing; therefore, you must cauterize the patient with two cautery irons. One in the root of the ear, the other at the temple, and the third at the junction of the two eyebrows. Place the cautery iron in the part that opens well and make it cauterize at the head of the ear below the tip of the earlobe, and another at the temple as long as one eye. And leave the cautery iron in place until half of the hair is burnt; this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the semblance of a cutlass that we have placed before you, but it is a more subtle and effective remedy than the knife; after treating like this, as I have said before, until it is healed.

de litargie	De litargie.

When lying down. de la froidor dou chief	From the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit. de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The fiery cautery must not be used except in cases of phlegmatique inflammation; and first of all modify the head of the year and other treatments that we have mentioned in the preceding chapter when the patient is large and suffering from excessive medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit. Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feeble, make one subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie. After that, take the patient’s chief; then make a circle of lint well made, like a circle, and put it on the chief; and hold the patient’s limbs crossed, and keep them well secured from all sides; then bring the flame and burn a little barley chaff; and keep the fire temperate so that the patient can tolerate it; then remove the circle from the chief and let it cool; do this for the patient once every week with another good government, until he is healed.</start_of_turn>
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see the burnings made by doing more pricks all over the cautery.

de l’awe des eulz	If you see the burn cauterized by making several pricks throughout the burn. This method of cautery soothes the brain instantly; then put on moist cotton wool in butter and lard.

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	For the pain of tears through the eyes,

de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is as follows in this manner

Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.

Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the mark that you have made, and doing this several times, so that the burn is neither too deep nor too shallow; and the sign of the work is that you see the membrane withdraw, and the hair is raised to the point of the oil; then you should keep your hand still, and let them rest for two days; then put a moist cloth in butter until the swelling has gone down; after that, apply an ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs grow, and the papere is softened, then restart the cautery on the same place as before; and if the hairs are plucked out, burn them as long as the papere returns to its natural state, and be even, and do not prick the hairs with the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make parchment of the shape of a bay leaf; then take soap of France and live chalk, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it thick, so that it does not reharden, then put it on the shape that you have made like a bay leaf, and put the papere on the eyes; and if the disease persists in oil only, you must open in oil only, and if in both; and put cotton wool soaked in oil around the wound; and the head of the shoulder must be in its natural position and your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once and let it move every time the patient feels a biting of the medicine, for he feels biting just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has reached your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite is passed, if lift the limb of the shoulder, and reward if you see the skin raised as much as it was raised by the contraction of the fire or by incision; and if it is still, it is well
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, if you recall any medicine from before or the medicine has not worked, as long as your works are equal and your eyes are fixed; then put on a moist cloth in the burrow until the hairs are gone, and afterwards cure the wound which is called "dyafenis" and others, as long as they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you are confident that you can manage your work well with great care that it does not require any medicine, as your eyes remain fixed
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the wound becomes soft after it has bled, and the hair pricks in the oil, if you start the medicine again on that limb which has softened due to the wound, as you did before; afterwards cure until it is healed; this is the way of the fuelle of the myrtle tree.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	Know that the souls of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to that are your constraints; and do not be afraid to take another way to that which is studied by this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment brings no benefit, then you must cauterize according to this manner
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to hold his head still; and hold his ears between your hands in such a manner that he does not move them, does not lower his head; then put a wet cloth or vinegar juice on the oil; then burn the cautery which is partly: and keep it over the head as if it were a goose feather; gather up what has been cauterized if you see it, if there is a point from the one ear to the other; and if you see that there is a burn similar to a burn; but whatever happens, that which is over the head is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula until it is over, and draining the pus, and drying; and if it is closed, if the wound, and drain the wound; then put the cautery on hot and hold your hand over the cautery at the part of the thumb next to the oil, so that your hands do not tremble; and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and hold it firmly.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not suffice, if you repeat the cautery once more, and if you are in doubt, let it remain for three days; after that, put on moist wool in the wound and treat with desiccant ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and leave as it comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistula of which none of the ancients spoke.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a fistula, and open the cavity; then put into the opening I camel's hair as much as this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I make to the quantity of a third of an ounce; and hold your hand or gauze firmly, and do not move the patient, only that the melted wax does not come into contact with it; and it is advisable to put on the patient's oil a moist bandage of wool or cotton: the wax will thus adhere to the vessel of the fistula, and the patient will recover with great marvel at the health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if that does not happen, if it is necessary, one must perform a perforation on the nerve and restore the fistula to its proper place as it should be in the body.
des crevaices en levres	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if you must, administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its normal place as it should be in its proper place.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	If the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if you must, administer a perforation to the nerve, and bring the fistula back to its normal place as it should be in its proper place
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you have treated these cracks resulting from the divisions we mentioned, and the cure has not profited, then you should perform a small cautery culture according to this fashion:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated these cracks resulting from the divisions we mentioned, and the cure has not profited, then you should immediately perform a small cautery culture in that area until the pain ceases; after the cure, keep the limb still until it has healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the armpit.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes to the root of the arm or the elbow, or the shoulder or the root of the teeth, after making the opening and the wound becomes swollen and forms a fistula; and you should cure it as we have mentioned in the divisions, and it will not profit: so it is necessary that you have a small cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after you have cauterized the opening or perforation of the fistula, and keep your hand still until it has healed at the front and behind; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have mentioned in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, that is good; but if not, you must uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find in this chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have cured it with medicine, this is of no avail; therefore put the patient’s hand in your own; after that withdraw the cautery which will form afterwards in part as if you were putting on a pincer; and put the cautery into the tooth socket immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that withdraw your hand and resume the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and keep it closed for an hour and a quarter.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, when the teeth which were moving are confirmed, and the soft gum is restrained, and the moisture is corrupted, it dries up.
de la dolor des dens	De la douleur des dents.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures do not help, then it is necessary to perform cautery in two ways: cautery of the nerve and cautery of the fire.</start_of_turn>
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of the burn if such be that you grasp a burn of grease, and the end in a spoon of iron or pewter; after taking cotton and wrapping over the tip of a rag, and the boil in grease boils, and put upon the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cold; and do this often until the remedy comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see if there is still grease and cotton in the grease, and put upon the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery must be held as if one grasps a nail or an arachnids; let the fire not reach the patient’s mouth; after the fire has been kindled, lay the cautery on the tooth and hold the hand until the fire is cold; do this often, for the pain will be great as if from the same or the following day
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	One must ensure that the patient fills his mouth with good burr in the haste of this cautery, and then hold tight; and that is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery as you please, and according to what you have seen fit; and this is the form of the burn.
des scrophules	And the size of the wound on the thumb and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are any of these wounds or chieftains who have no moisture, and of these wounds which I cauterize or chieftains of an old woman; and find the wound just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no blood appears, we must make the wound just as well as if it were a stone. In other wounds coming or chieftains, forasmuch as these which come from the head of the fetus and have roots of the ears, the opening must be made every day to the most dependent part of the limb; and the cure must be made as it should be.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the lymph nodes are filled with phlegm and cold moisture, and are not subject to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the cautery needle beforehand; for two wounds will appear from the fumes to irritate the cautery of the other side; and place the cautery hot on the abscess once, or if it intermingles, until it reaches the front of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put in the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in place for three days; and put on a wet compress over the wound until the swelling has subsided.
Li forme de la cainne:	The formation of the abscess:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the veins due to cold complexion, it is necessary that the patient be first purged by dissolving medicines; after that, perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go down to the stomach, and do not go too deep but just a little bit
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, do another cautery at the joint of the collarbone at the head of the scapula; and let the cautery which is called the "clavile" be as we have the shape before; and cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and even when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medicines; afterwards perform the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go further than the throat, and do not burn more than is necessary. Afterwards perform another cautery at the joint of the collarbone at the base of the spine; and let the cautery which is called the "claw" remain as it is; and cure the limb as it has been said above until it is healed.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When moisture prevails over the pores and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and the ailment is ancient, if you perform two cauteries on the forcele [jaw] in the front and one between the two nipples; and let the cautery which is called the "claw" remain as it is as it has been said above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, do the cautery by pricking all the cautery which is called "points" because their form is like this in the ear disease; and let the points be up to XXX, or until bent.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After that, cure the limb as we have said above, and let the cautery be three times according to this form.</start_of_turn
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that, these cauteries are lighter, for these that you make at .iij. together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	because of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, support the patient on their back and chest; then take hold of the thumb which is within the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, if necessary, grasp the cautery which has about an inch of length: thus...
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	...and burn the thumb until it reaches the chest, and the burn would come out with three cauteries in total; and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery which has about two nails, for the figure of cautery is like two nails; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a thread and this is the form of the cautery which has about two nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is the suture placed upon this nerve because there are seven cauteries there.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then put on the cautery, broil the wounds with oil; then rest the patient, and do not move the limb until it is well comforted.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if there is a dislocation below, whatever the cause, then do the cautery on the thick part of the "clavile" cautery, or several pricks.</start_of_turn
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is bony, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When the stomach brings cold and moist humors as long as they stain its complexion, and multiply the diarrhea to it, these are customary cures and they do not help; therefore it is necessary that the patient rest on his back, extend his legs and arms.</start_of_turn>
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, make three cauteries: one on the heel, two on the hip bone for the amount of two nails; for every cautery mark, close the wound with a needle, and make two cauteries on the two costae as long as the figure of the cauteries is at a right angle, and has some space between each other so that they do not join together when they swell; and let the cauteries be so strong that they draw out the two parts of the bone, and let the figure of the cauteries be as described above.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see him cauterized with a great cautery in the stomach in this fashion; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach. As much as you see of the hair; then cauterize the remainder of the hair which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have seen before, while he is still conscious.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain of cold and moisture and great swelling, because it is forced out of its natural position by the humors; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and he does not profit from it, if he is not anointed on his navel; and sign of hair three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, to push away the spleen, the liver or the kidneys; and there be space between each cautery the thickness of an egg; and let the cautery be long as the nail of the thumb, and do not press too hard with your hand over the whole cautery; and let only half of the burn be visible, and the patient should lie on his side; and if he cannot, let him lie without moving, and extend his legs, and keep his arms crossed; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will be, if you cauterize these cauteries of little sweetness, if you are subtle and prudent in the art, and take care that you do not burn all the hair, for you will make it dry all over; and that it does not come out of its place, for the hair is very subtle in that place, and the nails will see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has burst into the liver, and you know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the gall: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels little pain; but if it is in the gall, the pain is violent.</start_of_turn>
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is finished, if you think the patient is cured of his head; then sign with the touch of the hand over the wound or the burst, and then burn the cautery which is like a thread, for this is its form.</start_of_turn
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And I cauterize thus far as the hairs are long and even, and come up until the root is strong; until the wound is fully healed; after that, cure as for ordinary wounds until they are healed; and I advise you that this cautery should only be used by one who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whom these diseases have never occurred before.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, he should not dare to work, and I think that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleura.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that we must make for pleuresin cauteries of root of aristologe, and in part thus: take a root of aristologe long, the greatest that thou shalt find, and be dry, and be as great and as long as thy two hands; and the grease in oil, and the mark on the fire, and cauterize. I. Cauterize between the nipple and the collar, and II. Two small cauteries in descending on that which is below the beard; and III. Cauterize between the fifth rib and the twelfth, declining behind a rib. I. Cauterize at the pit of the stomach, and I. Another above the stomach, and I. Between two ribs, and II. Have two ribs below the pit defend the cautery that is between two ribs; and do not press me your hand, but make it open as when smelling.

And they say that no ancient person uses a fire cautery resembling a razor, and the eschaufet and put between the ribs, until it comes to this incision; and great pain follows, as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver

de la mice	of mice
