Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter or bathe while the limb is slightly flexed, and then make him enter or lie down, and the pain will go away entirely and will be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And such matters that no one must use fire cautery for such medicines, except after the evacuation of bones.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And thus Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a piece of glass, if it is of little size; and must be done cautiously.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in much oil, and put it on the pit between the thumb and the great toe and the one that is called fossicle
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that take a piece of glass dry and burn it until it is charcoal, and put it on the lint, and leave it until it is stained; and do this again and do not stop doing this until you think that there is no more pain; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of glass".
de la dolor dou dos	of backache.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation of blood, or from similar symptoms of cold spreading matter, of none of these symptoms is the fire cautery of any value, save for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is devoid of stinking pills or other similar things, we must make three lines signed with a mark on the back, loin or where the pain is located; and make three or four cauteries according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery must be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see this, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that it has burst open in the loin when it comes on; and there is doubt and fear; and you find at the back of the spine on the back and on us its appearance which comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see that and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle according to this fashion.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery touches some part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	If you see that it has cauterized around the spine at the point where the cautery has pierced two or three lines, and that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound as far as it is necessary for it to be healed, according to what we have said above, and beware that you do not move the cautery over the nerve which is in close proximity to the wound
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when the pain originates from within the bone, it is called "podagre" properly. And when the cause is cold and the disease does not yield to medicines, it is often cured by cautery in this way: make a mark of the cautery around the joint of the limb, and apply the cautery as follows:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the bone, if you are to cauterize all the way through with the cautery, you must declare "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the joints and others, and this happens many times, if you are to cauterize each joint three times or four times on each part, with the olive oil; and if you must do more, do so, but do not keep your hand over the wound for longer than necessary until the sensation of pain has passed
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as far as the hands, if you make points at the navel two lines; and if there remains no pain at the navel, if you make points on the wrist and on the nail of the hand; and if the pains come down to the buttocks or down to the elbows, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient drink and take medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him drink and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the routure comes, and the bowel descends like stones and it is new, if you see that when you attempt to cure it, it does not mend itself; and that it causes things to leave the belly, so that the pain descends from the belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his shoulder tight until the bowel is repaired, and keep his arms at your sides, and mark with your finger the routure above the shoulderbone, and at any sign that it resembles half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is soft and evacuates sensation.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then restrain the bowels in their place; and he holds your hand so that they do not return backwards; and give the patient good compresses, and put a cushion under his hips and one under his wrists; then put the cautery on the sign at all your hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be wary that the bowels do not protrude when you are making the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that through this the patient does not die, or any other evil
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And as for wounds that do not reach the bone at the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you must know that the cautery of small wounds must be subtle in measure according to the quantity of hair, and that of great people also great in measure; after three days cure the abscess until the scab becomes bony; after that cure other matters until they are healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well healed; and you must know that its nourishment must be continuous, so that the boils do not come out when he stirs to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made broth, and let him rest for forty days; and give him good rest, that he work little and beware of too great drinking of wine and eating, and of too high a diet; and when he has learned this he will be completely healed
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the treatment of the heel in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the evacuation of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come out of other parts and are known, and you see that they do not grow further, if you do not cauterize them with the cautery, they will remain as much as before; after the treatment, as we have said; neither the former doctors have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place with ink and make a line along the width of the wound, and another at the bottom, and hold your hand firmly over the cautery needle
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more fluid.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, or the shoulder or the hip, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical treatment is not of use, then it is advised that it be cauterized with the cautery called “points,” and the cautery should be done according to the length of the limb, its thickness and weakness, its toughness and its tendency to twist and its pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is well after the first burn, it is good; if not, repeat the burn upon that one, for it is customary that it must move to the neighboring part, so that you can make the burns while the patient is well.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or from sitting, and the pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is recommended to cauterize the area using the cautery known as the "points." The cautery should be performed according to the length of the limb, its breadth, its weakness, its toughness, and its twisting and painfulness. If the first cautery is successful, well and good; if not, repeat the process. Indeed, it is customary to perform the cautery on the area that is closest to the painful area, so that one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases do not yield to burn once or twice with great aid, and even the diseases that come from the corruption of humors and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the burn being made? Take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, do not linger, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the illness, then make five burns on the head: one on the new head, and one at the front towards the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the cheek; and leave the hand as long as the burns come up to the bone, and as long as the scabs fall out so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and burn on the mouse according to what is before you
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if there is a mixture of moisture everywhere; and it appears openly, if you must use these cauteries that we have mentioned or chief, namely a cautery on the top of the thumb, two cauteries on the spine of the collarbone, three cauteries on the spine of the shoulder, one large on the elbow and one other elsewhere, two on the two thumbs, two on the scapulae, two on the flanks, two on the Achilles tendons, and one on any joint of the hands or feet, and on the pits of the hands; keep away from the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, so that you do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bones of the heel or the bones of the stomach or the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the wounds that when more fire cautery is made, more aid is given, and profit is made for him; and the wounds that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as when he feels it, because the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you find in the handling of herbs
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment with flour poultices several times with honey and other cures until they are healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and is not well, then make cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and let the cautery penetrate deeply as much as possible; then cure with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never do we cauterize at the hand, the foot, or the back, at the exit of nerves that move the limb, and thus if it is bony it swells; and in no way should anyone interfere unless they are skilled in limbs and the exits of the moving nerves from the bones.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is done to cauterize on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either the cautery is made at the root of the thumb or at the tip of the ring finger. Then it is cured with ointment until it is healed. And at no time is cautery done on the hand, foot, or back, at the issue of the nerve that makes the limb immobile, or if it is bony swelling. And all this is done without any hindrance if one is skilled in the limb and the issue of the moving nerves around the bone.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then it is done to cauterize with a needle once, according to the quantity of the area, until the swelling is bony and has changed colour; then it is cured with flour of times and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and without colocynth and alum, a part of each; and all this is mixed together, and bound up with a bandage, and left to heal until it is healed
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil first appears, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the circumference that seems like a circle, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that we must cauterize also in the middle of the boil; and in no way does it seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it is better to leave it alone; and the right thing is to cauterize around it, at the cautery which is called the "circle", as we have said before.</start_of_turn
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has an ailment called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or because of the excessive heat it causes or because of the excessive blood in the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old), or because of foul air; and you see that it is urgent to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; and leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turn with the entire cautery, if it is hot, cauterize the cautery again so that this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this ailment called "adubelati" until the cauteries have perceived the cold, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels a tingling sensation in part as the process progresses.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Leave it thus until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another disease that is called "corrodens" is nothing but the softening of limbs, for it causes the limbs to swell up like dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb which can suffer from fire cautery, then shave the hairs closely with small and large clippers, as it is suitable for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains except for the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs, let them be broiled with oil until the burnt hairs are ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that secrete pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hair does not grow back, it is good; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupt.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This remedy is never sufficient to cure a medical ailment in place of fire cautery; but all the same, fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when a wound has festered, a disease called "clos" appears according to our understanding, which is a large and burdensome burden that makes the patient weep blood from the wound
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	The cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	If you burn with fire, if you are rash, I burn the hair in like a needle of wool; it is made of good iron of the measure that it can penetrate the head of all parts, and there must be subtle margins; after that put all around on the head of the hair, and twist your hand all around the head until it comes to the front of the head; and leave it there for three days until it begins to soften; then make an embolus of wild mallow seeds with silk, and leave the embolus on all night, and close the wound tightly and it will be scraped from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of swelling by applying pressure until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if there are converts by boils, and many times happen and in hands and in feet, if you can consider that you must bring an aquaplast of hot water; and it is in part like this: take a hazel or iron pin or a needle of wool, and put it on the wound and the clot; that is to say, poke the warts; and put the hazel on so that it tightens all around, then put a little bit of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while the margin of the hazel comes to the root of the wound, and can find the hot water way deep until the root; and give the patient a little sip of the hot water an hour; then leave it like that, and it will discharge all at its roots
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So make another, until you have scraped all these things from the bone, then cure the wounds which are caused by hair.
li cure dou trembler	You have not provided any text for me to translate, so I am unable to provide a translation.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When the body trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever or from another, if you make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery at the waist and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them on, the trembling will cease and the patient will be cured of the cold.
des pustules puans	When the body trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever or from another, if you make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery at the waist and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them on, the trembling will cease and the patient will be cured of the cold.

si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.

Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the limb is restored; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and take notice that when without displacement of an artery, it is not possible to fill it up properly even when the artery is large, except by one of the three methods that we have mentioned: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by strong ligation of thread, or by medicines placed upon it that have power to restore blood flow. And let it be firmly held in place afterward.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb violently with cloths or with the laying on of burning things, or other similar things, if it does not prove helpful, does harm.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines. Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag li secons livre des cures de taille.

Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.

Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	I advise you only to do what those tell you who have this custom, but put more caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but thoughtfully of what you are certain, and of what you have already taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either converted or continued; and this will help you to obtain good fame, glory, and memory over time.</start_of_turn
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you must understand and rejoice, and if you yearn to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.

Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I once saw a child in whom the bone was completely split with pain, and the head grew so much that it could not bear; and I believed that the moisture was so great that it would kill the patient, and when it is collected between the bone and the flesh, between the marrow and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the marrow and the bone, and the incision is small, you must make a wide cut; and as long as the moisture remains, the form is like that of a spasm
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, following this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture swells the bone, and the sign that you see the head of the bone protrude from the chest, and it sharpens when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not return: if you suspect that the head of the bone is fractured, you must make two incisions as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out the moisture with all your might.

de reume	When the bone is fractured or the vein is opened, and the cavity is filled with liquid, do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; let the blood flow freely, for if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease which is called a "catarrh" which has pus or blood, and the disease is ancient, and the medicine does not profit, then the only cure is to cauterize with that which will not cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary to do this, for if you see the patient raise his head; after he has rubbed his limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then draw out the patient’s head from under the dressing; then look to see if the vein is open, and if so, put in two needles at the two ends of the vein, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, and this is done by grasping the head of the vein with the thumb and index finger.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see it, hold the sponge below the artery and close the wound above, cutting as much as .ij. inches across the middle.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is closed, if blood spurts continuously, stop it immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee. de emigrainne	And if the artery does not open on feeling, if you know that two fingers’ breadth will suffice, mark the spot and proceed until bone; what may be forced out with blood should be done so if it be more than two fingers’ breadth, and less if possible. According to what the patient can bear and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point where the stitches were placed, if the tape that was put around them has not held, then strain the wound and tie it up, and treat it with oil until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes with acute catarrh, because of the tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient sode are lost and similar things, and it is treated by means of medical cures and all that does not benefit, except for the cauterization of the arteries of the temples.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus the method of extracting them is that if the patient makes the hair of his temples grow long, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not put back as quickly as in some men who are too cold; and if it is put back, the patient must raise his head from some covering, then rub the limb with no rough cloth, and pour cold water over it until the artery opens clearly; then take the spatumile, which is its shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then loosen the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up as high as the nails, and remove the hair well from the area that is below the armpits; and if the artery is small, if the nail has at the tip of the elbow, then cut that part according to the quantity of two fingers.</start_of_turn>
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not held firmly, if it leaps out without warning in every way.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And pull out blood from the groin to the elbow, just as much as is necessary; and if the artery is large, it is convenient to bind it with two strong threads of silk, so that no blood will appear in front of the wound, and let the blood drain naturally; then cut away the surplus that is between the two threads in that place, and if you see that, if you wish, you can cauterize with a cautery needle until the hair is cut off; and that is the best remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is useful for finishing off moisture: because of this it is of more use against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is useful to extract the arteries that are filled with much cotton and put on well-made bandages; and when you remove them, if you are cured of dry medicines that cause the growth of hair and bandages, as long as you are sane; and if you do not have a staunch for the artery as you should when you cover with cautery, or you use the hand of vitriol and strain it from your hand, which is without stain; and if you do not have that, if you must remove the limb, you must do so until it is frozen, and rise the limb with cold water until it stops, and strain it as it should be strained; and what is more tender and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting through a third part, but the cutting should be well spaced to ward off more length of heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tense, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with needles, let the loop of the forceps burn over until it reaches the bone, and grasp the vein with the forceps; and keep the bones separated from each other because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.
des larmes	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch. Then, when you have marked the area with needles, let the loop of the forceps burn over until it reaches the bone, and grasp the vein with the forceps; and keep the bones separated from each other because they are not soldered by this cautery in any way. This is the form of the fire cautery.

When the tears of the eyes descend from veins that are above the root of the head, and it does not profit any medical cure in doing so, and you see the patient’s face swell up, and feel pain in his front and gait like a madman; and although they are tense and moist if paper towels are placed over them, and are shaken off by the heat of the tears, if there is no other remedy for this cure.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the swelling of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes swelling of the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or stone or other foreign bodies; or seed, as in cases of peas, beans, or barley; or a flowing liquid as in the case of fever and chills and other things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it hurts in the earlobe or any other way that does not seem to agree with the ear, do not put it under pressure, if put the ear to the sun.

Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times blood comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, order the extraction of fine pins, for this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If the stone comes out by itself, that is good; if not, prepare for extraction with small needles of double curvature; and if it does not come out by this, take a pinch of the flesh and tear a part of the ear very little, and stop the bleeding that comes from the wound with wax if necessary; then the pain will go away, for many times it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take hold of the flesh around the wound and press on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in a hurry to make an incision at the ear base as well as at the apex of the chalazion vein, and if there is spasm, do not hesitate to make the incision first at the front of the head; then draw the patient’s head between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fatty tissue or bone depending on which is easier; and let the vein bleed out as much as necessary, and evacuate the pus from the wound until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is grains that are swollen and inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, administer sponge-rubber according to this form:

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the swelling of the ears.

de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the pus.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The grease called exinach is enclosed in papers of parchment which are wet, and this is more effective against certain people who are envious; it causes great moisture to their eyes, and from this comes the tearing of the morning; and they cannot look at the light of the sun because of this, for the tears hurry to their eyes; and because of this they lie with their faces down, and sleep, and the papers of parchment are wet on their eyelashes which causes them to swell and appear covered with exinach which breaks out in oil.

Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the vein being cut, if the cure for the swelling is to drain as much as is sane.
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper is born with hair attached other than its natural state, and is enclosed, if it irritates the eyes, it causes various diseases like tears and softening of paper and glue, as well as the destruction of the eyes; the cure for this is in three ways: either by applying cautery with fire, or by medicine with water, according to what is before or alongside the cautery, or by incision and suture or by thread, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient’s head in your left hand, then pull the paper from the oil at your left hand side; if it is converted, that is good; if not, if there is an awl at all.i. thread from above; either cut the margin of the paper or the hair will be pulled out; then take one thread from below and pass it through all the paper, and pull it out at the scraper; then make in the lower part of the paper, from the bottom of the hair, the hair that is attached, with all the surrounding fat, from the great tear until the little one; then draw out one thread and put under the paper a little fold of cotton and bandage, and sign on the paper a figure like a mistletoe berry, and it is sufficient that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevate the paper which is assigned to you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it comes to the vein being cut, if the cure for the swelling is to drain as much as is sane. If there is much discharge of purulent matter from the wound, as much as two lines below the wound, and from the great toe to the little toe; and let there be a puncture mark at the root of the hair, then insert the ligature at one of the two angles downwards, then draw the ligature tight; then suture the two layers together with a fine needle and silk thread, and dry the wound, remove the excess thread from around the two edges, as you see that it must be done; and if this does not succeed, leave the suture and the thread for three days or four; then cure the wound by stitching with dry and constricting things, because the pus will return to the bottom of the wound and reunite the edges, but the suture is useless (as the old people say), and that is dangerous; and if there is another method: let the patient sign the pus with a mark that is like the berry of a myrtle, as we have heard, at three inches distant according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cover what is above with small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you cannot hold the teeth firmly, and the matter is not equal, take a needle or two and pass one thread through the great loop and the second thread through the small loop, and gather the two threads evenly; then stretch your hand evenly, and stretch all the skin above where you have marked, as we have told; then gather the two layers of the wound together with sutures, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and similar soothing ointments. Never again shall you find that the hair of the papilla has been converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the sutures in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for carbuncles is as follows: convert the beard hair and the hair of the head according to what has been said, and then make two incisions each as long as the beard and wide enough for two fingers; and take two threads of the same length as the beard. Then assemble one to the other securely over what rests on the beard oil, and strain the two carbuncles from the two ends; and leave it in place for a few days. The skin that has been strained will become soft and wrinkled and will disappear, as long as it is treated by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and when the papilla has risen, the hair will no longer grow; and this is the form of two nails you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is like taking a subtle needle, and there is i.e. a silken thread; then gather the hairs and do not let one touch another subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not knot the chief of the thread; then put the patient's chief in its place; and let there be sunlight so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then withdraw the needle throughout the chase to the root of the hair, and make it bleed profusely until you have bled out all that is natural; then remove the hair until there is only one or two or three or more remaining; then remove your hand as much as the vein escapes throughout the chase with the natural flow of blood.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not bleed with it, if you draw the chase to a close with all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein bursts from the root and you see it through the sight of the oil; then if you draw the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has bled out and the burden has ceased; and if the hair is small, if you accompany it with a long thread of natural wool, and leave it until it is elongated and then take it away.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes into being, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there follows from a wound, or a burn, or a cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	The way of working in this is that you make the wound close, dry the flesh, put in some flaxseed, and keep it until it is healed; and do not do anything but use for its treatment things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, if the disease returns worse than before; but there is need of softening things, as with rue or chamomile; and vinegar or salt and poppyseed and mustard seed boiled in no oil, and they enclose a bandage, and treat it thus
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have said is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not come back differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the cauldron that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called «axacrati» is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	This disease arises from wounds and cuts and burnings and similar things; and the cause of this ailment is that if you take an awl, because it has two edges, and the point in the flesh, and it causes the left cheek to swell so much that the vein is split in two at the height of the cheek; then the cheek is raised up to the awl, and there is a large wound at the awl's point.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound returns as it should, that is good; but if not, take a saw and place it in the wound, and turn the wound, and make two incisions or break two bones in the wound; and if there are two incisions from two angles of the incision that you have made, make one angle so that when they are put together, the figure looks like the letter that has no ‘I griesche’; then break that bone according to the quantity of its costae and the degree of swelling, of what has caused the wound, then join the two broken parts with a thread of silk; then apply the remedies that we have mentioned of mollifying medicines and bands, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the sickness comes from a fracture or a suture or from cautery, then it must be made that you make a clean incision all around the hairs of paper; and as for what is above, separate between the two books of a thumb, as I have said; and must be done according to the form of the sickness, for it is diverse in form, and the learned men appear to know everything from head to foot how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is suitable for the work and for the instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the sickness comes from a fracture or a suture or from cautery, then it must be made that you make a clean incision all around the hairs of paper; and as for what is above, separate between the two books of a thumb, as I have said; and must be done according to the form of the sickness, for it is diverse in form, and the learned men appear to know everything from head to foot how to restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is suitable for the work and for the instruments in various arrangements.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this fracture has occurred at the shoulder joint in such a manner that the limb hangs suspended with the palm downwards, and is unable to move or perform its natural functions, if it must be that you extract the bone from the palm of the hand, and elevate it upwards; and that the edges be bound together, as long as the surrounding skin is not too tight and does not tear the oil; and that your incision, which you have made to reassemble, be slight, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and that all that has been reassembled be bound together, and that no more oil be added to the wound, but only a little sweet water and vinegar; and after that put between the limb and the oil a cloth of linen, and cover with oily wool in abundance; and finally put on a bandage of wool and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Saiches that the nail is in two manners: it is nervous and seems like tough fat, and another which is not very nervous, but seems like white moisture frozen, that when it is touched with iron and is cooked through, there are pinpricks; and both seem to swell towards the great tear, and rise up so much that they cover the whole eye and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his hand in his bosom, then grasps the eyes; and keep your hand on his wrist, and then break the nail with pinpricks of small double curvature, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put in one hair of horse, or of sheep, or of beef, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle once and fix it in the nail, and pierce through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and support all around the nail the cost of the nail that surrounds the nail-bed and the hair to the hair just as far as the chief, and then close the remaining part in the root of the tear with all the small forces, and leave the natural tear or the tear itself; and in no way stretch the nail only with the needle and the thread, as we have said; then support all around the nail the surrounding area that is this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle does not pierce it; and after the incision, pour oil a little ball of butter, and give him a decoction of alum, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is left of it until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push back the needle, and the thread does not pass through, many times it is cured of this semblance of nail; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you pour oil on the patient, and take the sponge more slight in this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail gradually, and if you see that it does not decrease point and that the edge is pressing, if you distill from your mouth into the oil decoction of alum and red alum and butter, and pour oil until the other side; then repeat the other work as before, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and cure the abscess first while it is healthy, then resume the work as before, while it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If there appears fat floating in the oil at night, with great swelling, if you suspend it in vinegar, and cut off a part and not the whole, that blood does not rise; then distill in the red oil of colera, which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes from the navel.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary to nourish the cure with a weak oil of natural origin; and in an accident, in the work of fire; and do not burn your hand in any of these works until you see that the limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red that are covered with oil, and endure the gaze of the eye and burn the oil throughout the days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The master must first look at the oil when it is placed on the wound, for indeed the wound is fierce, and there is no other disease stronger than the wound; therefore the master should take hold: instruct the patient to put his head in order, then suspend the veins throughout their length as he deems fit, and be double-handed as much as he can in this fashion:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two veins by degrees in one limb according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then suspend these veins gradually by degrees in one limb according to this form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of this in that hour, make a poultice on the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is relieved and is secure from after-pain; then begin again according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and that is the way of the forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect all of this in that hour, make a poultice on the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is relieved and is secure from after-pain; then begin again according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and that is the way of the forces.
