de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not fierce but like water which is gathered in oil, resembling a descending wound, and it is not actually a wound; and the manner in which it appears is that you make the patient sit on a comfortable and straight chair, and take hold of the chief between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the water coming down towards your eyes; then either bind it tightly and do not let it go down or break the light, and see the patient do the things as he wanted; and if it does not go down after that, say that it is like a wound, and that when the water goes down it is not visible as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la char sor le neis	From the armpit on the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee. If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has been made with too little force, if nothing settles; and if it swells without stopping, or if it hangs loose, or if it is an abscess, then grasp it firmly as if it were possible; and if it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize it while it is not stained and all the pus has gone, then throw or pull out the contents easily and with speed or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he does not wish to work, and moisture comes to his palace, the nails that were once sound; if moisture does not pierce as it should, nails that are in the bone below, because the instruments do not come down to the root: therefore it is necessary that you put in one thread of linen a good inch, and grasp it with your hands, and leave between each nail an inch or less; and put the patient’s hand with the thumb at the bottom, and press so that it comes through the mouth; and many times they do this to the children, and it is a light thing for one who has seen it done; then take the chief that comes from the thumb to a hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth to the other hand, and pull one after the other until they are even with us who are holding.

de la char sor le neis	From the armpit on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the neck a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes very great all of a sudden, so that it is visible to see; and for this reason it is commanded that you should begin to compress it at the beginning, and break the bone thoroughly, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in compressing it when it is great, if you take hold of it firmly, from a dark color to a pale hue, if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a thorny abscess, for when you touch it even once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, you can see that you can easily compress it, if you leave the patient and compress it without fear, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do as much as you can until you are certain that the cartilages that are causing the continuation of the disease have been cured; then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam; and reinsert it as before. Repeat this for three days or more, until the cartilages have eaten away everything that remains of the disease; then put in or withdraw a cauterizing sponge for a certain number of days until it is healed, and if there is need for sedatives, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, for from it are distilled the oils and medicines or not.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it happens for no reason that the wound is fresh throughout its entirety; then join the two layers to a rib, and hold them together until they are healed; and if the layers are already detached from one side and the other, then you must support all the parts around it until they heal, and reassemble the two layers to a rib, and hold them, and sprinkle upon them powder of dragon's blood and incense; and put upon the powders a piece of dressing of strong or another dressing that will stick, and leave it until it discharges by itself, and cure it of oozing until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of making the bolster is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the belly bolster; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the detachments of the fingers.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of a master, the book has teeth like sharp grains of wheat, minor and greater; thus it is right that you must break the teeth, open each socket, and take them as pincers and grasp in the front part; then apply the paste after the incision of the vitreous membrane, until it is dry; and then remove it easily, and cure the part with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the root of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times blood appears on the teeth of the gums, which are often called "albules"; if you hold them steady and grasp their root, and let the blood flow out or the blood clot; then put out the vitreous membrane, or other drying and restraining powders; and if the gum comes back after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize: if it does not come back even after the cautery; these are the signs of the instruments that cover it.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are assembled at the chief of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, teeth which are lazy and dull; and never are the teeth black and yellow and hollow, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head is straight, and open the teeth or the gums open, until nothing remains; and then make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if that has happened at the first reason, it is good; if that has not happened, if you repeat the second and third time, until you have done everything; and the teeth that have to be extracted have various forms of instruments to remove them, as that which the work shows, because the raisers of the teeth which one must withdraw have other forms than those which one must put between the teeth; and these forms and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you later withdraw as much as you wish, because it must not make me do it; for it is a substance that is very bitter, therefore we have no excuse for neglecting to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained to do something against his will, then you must be certain that he will obey.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient groans in pain, and cares whether it is great or little, and makes him groan; and all this while the pain does not depart from him because of the illness, for we have already wanted to do this to these scoundrels; and when you are certain that he will obey, then you must support the limb firmly to protect the joint from all sides; then move the limb to and fro at the first part and part, until it is well dislocated; and then firmly grasp the nails. And let the patient groan between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, stretch the tooth directly forward until it snaps; if it does not snap, take none of these instruments and hold it loosely in the cheek, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and bent, if you can, fill it with cloth, lace or gut; and if you strain it gently, do not break it while straining; and must cautiously wipe around the gum with a scraper for the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient by the severity of the root, more pain than before.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware that you do not do what the ignorant healers do, who break the limb every time without any reason, and do not bring any benefit to anyone; but they cause many to die from the root of this great disease from the fractures that they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if blood comes, which often happens, apply a piece of vitriol; if that does not suffice, cauterize.</start_of_turn>
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, indeed mute them at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large size if they do not bend while drawing, and be of iron well made, and be tipped with teeth to hold.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains immobile at the shoulder, if you must put out the wet cotton swab that is in the wound, do so with care lest you break the bone.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is flexible, because there are teeth that are hidden "algis", which makes the head of the shoulder appear like a beak; and they must be removed in the same way as with a lime, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the bark entirely around the root, and place the instrument which is called "althali," which is to say a palainche, from which it is known.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and firm so that it does not break me, and if the root leaps up by this, that is good; if not, if you aid me with all your instruments, from which these forms will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, from which it is known.
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form: let it be known that this instrument is so strong that it cannot break, and its jaws like those of instruments for teeth; and with other instruments which are not mentioned here; the master surgeon will himself find the instrument which is appropriate for each case, according to what his work and the disease demonstrate, for there are many diseases for which the old methods do not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it breaks at the root of the bone or any other bone, or if it moves, if it seeks these instruments that it must be used, as I have said, and to aid it with gestures, for this is its form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be known that it must be strong and well-held to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but that it can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine that is appropriate for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, if the grasp has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural curve, and the form is bad, even in women of fair complexion, if one should know that it is necessary to extract it since it cannot be saved or comforted: then one must remove it; and if it is close to the tooth, take hold of this instrument which is like a small beak, and if it is of iron without a groove at the top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the socket often swells and swells up in the hands for the duration of the tooth, and because of this one does not move the others, and if it appears one can limber it if one files a piece of the file to the shape of this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like when one files nails; and while filing the tooth slightly, if it does not move too much, when the work is finished at the end there is no rasp, and when it is dense enough it bites the tongue, so if one limps the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, or by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot bear the weight of these things without groaning, and you must cure them with restrictive medicines, this is of no use; for if you must restrain them with a golden thread, because the silver thread turns green and becomes foul, but the blood does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, if you take hold of the thread and pass it double between the two front teeth, then put the head of the tooth between the teeth mentioned above, if there is one or more of them, until you see it is straight up to the sound tooth on the other side; and then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, until it does not move; and let your thread be fixed to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the humerus with one hand and the other hand gather the bones together, and put them back between the teeth; and hold them so that they do not slip; and let them rest as much as they can, and if they slip or the bone is fractured, if the strain of another bone; if it should remain and serve its purpose, and this is the form of a tooth and the figure of the arrangement of the two upper teeth and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of whalebone, and put it back in the place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it tight and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes the cause of loosening the tongue or the jaw is not birth, or by an accidental wound; and the work is such as you would offer the mouth of the patient, and take hold of the tongue, and then grasp the large nerve, until the tongue is freed from its place. If there is duration or difficulty, and this is an indication of a wound, if there is swelling and grasping of the large nerve; and keep the wound from being too deep, for the artery that is loosened; and when you have done this, if you lift the limb of water warm and easy, or cold water, and then put the tongue back in its place with a slight tension; and hold the patient’s hand tight, so that the limb cannot move.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows from a vein, take out the clot with a forceps; and if it does not go away, cauterize with the blunt cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see pus color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a sore; and if it is declining to swell, and there is moisture, if it evacuates the clot, and you wipe with a fine sponge, and deliver from a part and from another; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a broiled vitriol until it is dry, and then return to your work until you have finished all the work; then lift the limb easily and gently, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes blood flows from the gullet, which is called a "godath", and the swelling has two almonds in size; when you treat them, as we have said previously, and they are not healed, beware: if it is a hard abscess of little size and dark colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron; but leave it alone until it is dead, and then you will take it out, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a pale colour and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover it, but look first whether the abscess is firm and calm
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his head be upright, and hold his tongue with your thumbs between his hands, and press the tongue downwards to its entirety; for thus is the form. And be of silver or gold as subtle as a needle.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... and you see the boil, take the sponge and press it into the abscess, and hold it firmly for more than you wish; and do not pull out any hair with your fingers, then put the cover on the instrument, as it is formed, which looks like a force; and if the chief is crooked, and one place is higher than the other, and they are very painful, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with tenailles, know that this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with tenailles, know that this is the shape: cut an almond from one side and the other; and when you have grasped one almond, grasp the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and if blood appears, gargle the patient with hot water, or extract pomegranate seeds or rue marigold, or similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure as long as it is healed; and never again does an abscess appear in the throat except for the two almonds, if you grasp them just like the two almonds always.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had a severe constriction in her throat, so that she could neither breathe through her nose nor drink or eat, and she would have died if she had lingered in that state for a moment or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two stones through two holes that were not there before
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I took hold of her again, and put one hand on her incision, then I pulled her out, and pulled out a great piece of flesh; then I put the other hand in the other hole that was not there before, and I closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I put the incision back into the abscesses, and closed one part, and only a little blood escaped; and when I had stopped the bleeding from the vein, the woman began to drink water and then wine, and she continued to spit out of that abscess for a long time; and the abscess came back to its place and filled up her body as much as I had taken out; then I bound it and cauterized it inside her throat: and when I had finished with these parts, only God knows what happened to her afterwards
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb descends at the shoulder, and it flees and is elongated, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is broad and round, it is called "shoulder".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is sutured as we have said in the division, and the suture does not profit, and you see that the wound has healed, and it is subtle, if it is necessary, you must close it; and that which is round and compact and is not elongated; and that is bloodstained or reddish or black, if you must avoid the incision of the latter.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to what I have said, with its color and its length, you must make the patient sit in the sun, and stretch the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned before; then insert the ointment into the limb, and pull it out, and close with two sutures that I have mentioned in the incision of the two nipples.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must know that you should not cover more than the superfluousness which is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, you will grieve the voice and the words; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, you must know that you should use something to support the cautery in the painful area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cautery must be gentle and not severe
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in a comfortable position, and then press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned or the treatise of cautery, and hold it with a live hand, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, as it is formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. And if there is a hair or something put on the medicine, as the hairs of a spoonful, put the instrument on all the medicine above the navel; and the patient should be sitting on his cost, so that he salivates and the mucus comes out of his mouth from the medicine inside, if it does not go down to the throat, and the coughing; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the navel, the amount of half an hour, until you see it limp and the biting of the medicine is appeased; and if you see that, take cotton and wrap it over any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and withdraw the instrument with all the cotton in the cautery, until the cotton is burned on the navel; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and clean the cautery after three or five days. And if you must restart the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the navel with cotton wool, and cover what is around the medicine; and be raised with cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, for it is treated by fumigation according to this method. Take camomile, rue, origanum, ivy, cloves, and vinegar and assemble them all or any of them in a pot. Put some oil in it and boil. The pot must be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot is a tool that should be hooked according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or of gold, or be it one of the bones broken in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye by the caning, until the eye is mortified; after that, repeat often, until the eye is dry, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the event of the hot cautery, for many things will happen; and do not do this unless the hot cautery is declining.

And if this instrument is not present, if you take a caning and put within the head a speck of egg, so that the patient’s mouth is not too hot; for the speck of egg does not make the vapor rise up through the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether.

de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all may go well, do not push the bone inwards; and it is better that the patient move the instrument, because it is either stiff or the matter is putrefying; if the epiglottis is swollen, or if it is forced out with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.

puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet. li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeon of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The symptoms of boils are, as it is remembered in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which they appear, one of which is similar to the other, and the other due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And thus it is for the legs or if they are bound.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the afterpains of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the afterpains of the bone joint are different from those that come at the joints, and the bones judge in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if the afterpains must not be perceived, as long as the limb hangs limply; but if there are such things as must be perceived when they are stiff, and do not hang limply, as with an afterpain that is beyond the joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when the afterpain comes from the joints, and it is left as long as it hangs in tension, by chance if the limb is fractured and the nerve of the joint is ruptured, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the incision is made too high on the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is measured, it will go to the principal member; or if it is made too low, if you do not pierce it when it is measured, it will cause fistula.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you take out the pus of the abscess that is dead according to its companion; when the pain is calmed, the swelling has gone down, the redness and the heat have disappeared, the throbbing and the pain in the head of the abscess, and other signs; and that you make the perforation or drain the abscess more dependent on the abscess, and the place where it is; and that the perforation is long enough for the abscess that is at the hands or feet, or in the joints and nerves and arteries, and for all the bones that are equal or there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to this member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the incisions are in flesh, if the puncture is delayed until it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said

For if you pierce it before this, if it has become prolonged, it swells the body with poison and is full of bad breath; and by chance you harden the flesh and deepen the wound of it.

Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never has it happened in the belly and nowhere else, and is a disease which is called "fungus" because of its appearance like a foot, and is the root which is subtle, and the head is large; and there are some small and some large drops. I saw a man who had two or three of these in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were split open, and corrected the moisture accordingly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw them [fungs] and found in one XVIII ounces weight, and in the other VI and a third, and the work in the incision if it is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and has a thick root; if it reaches the large spleen, and if it is in your presence, do the cautery with fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the armpit, there often comes too great a discharge of blood; if it does not go away, if you haste, then do you burn; and if you see the patient groaning and fainting from the incision of the flesh, take a good thread of silk and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then bind it, and do not cease to drain the thread of silk until it stops the bleeding; and ask it from him how he feels. If the roots are exposed, if he has fear of the same on the other side, but take care to cover half of it, then burn it so that it does not return; then cure the wound and keep only that part which is of dark colour and little sense and milk-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess that is inflamed, and I will come to the cure of the abscess later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the shoulder is swollen it is painful.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If swelling appears, it comes from burn of wound or split of bone, and is on the belly and in the flanks of some blood, as it happens in other ways, or blood that clots in veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is by the route of the bone and by the discharge of the bowel, if it is the colour of the abscess, it is a slight thing with little pain, and opens from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	When it comes from the discharge of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with the hands, if it returns and comes back, and by chance if it is caught, and grows out with water and great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and open easily when you press it with your hand; do not constrain me. And if it is due to blood, if it is open by these signs, the abscesses are great and hard, and are fixed according to quantity. And if it is due to air, if it is blown towards the toucher, and the work if it is that you see that it appears due to the blood of an artery or a vein, or air.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or as the chapter says, concerning the abscesses of the artery and the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears due to the intestine or the spleen, if you must command the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out straight, then mark with your finger all around the belly; then command him to grasp between your hands, and bring towards the middle of your belly that which you have marked at the greatest circumference; then bind the other half of the abscess with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and if necessary we shall tie it; then open half of the abscess and bring your thumb and index finger to the navel, and look at the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, if you pull it out, bring the intestine out through the belly; and if you find the spleen, if you grasp it at the navel, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or the vein is making you do the opposite, if it goes well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and bring two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have made in the cross that you made to pierce; then strain the abscess for three periods over the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the limb until it swells, and cut the dead tissue by itself; or you can drain it when it is small and swollen, and cure it in the way that we have said; and stretch the abscess as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and close the limb.</start_of_turn>
dou chancre	And draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the cause of this that is causing it, and bandage the limb.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division concerning the signs of the chancre, and how one must treat it with medicine, and how one must shun the treatment of fire; and we say that the chancre is like a tumor in the marrow, and has great caution in its treatment, and the old men say that when a chancre is in the bone or can be pulled out like a tumor in the marrow, and in the flesh, and similar things, and it must be completely eradicated when it is in its beginning; but when it is great and old, if one cannot approach it, for I know of no cure for it; nor have I ever seen it cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And as for the work, when it is in the bone or can be pulled out, as we have said, you must purge the black bile from the patient once; then make it whole if it shows any swelling; then drain the patient; that is, give him good liquid to make the work; then extract your nails or the tumor, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts, without leaving anything in place; and leave the wound open, and press your hand or anything else firmly against it, and if the blood flows from the artery or vein, do not cauterize it too much lest it be stained; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Nos avons dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et celle qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let the incisions be of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let the incisions be of two parts, a point, and let them not be made too deep lest they reach the intestines when they are sutured, and do not clot them; then look if the bile is lodged towards the intestines: if so, make three sutures on the left side of the wound; and if the bile is due to the disease of the liver, make the incision on the left side of the wound; and if it is due to the spleen, make it on the right side, and do not make them deeper than necessary for the patient to rest on the incision that the fluid does not flow from that weak limb; then pierce all the leather with the instrument, and draw out the thread, and keep your hand over the wound as wide as from the nail to the wrist as when you are grasping the quantity of an nail or as much as an inch in diameter; then pierce the skin as wide as the width of your thumb, and that is the limit of the water, then withdraw the instrument, and there is your wound.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is like a silver coin turned upside down, and is of barley or barley straw lighter, and has at the upper part a little hole; or it costs one part, three holes; and two of another part, and one of another; and the head of the shoulder is cut off like a nail, and this is the form of the incision which the writer makes to cut off the nail.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the marrow, if when the instruments come to the point of sharpness, if it is now on the instruments; empty out then half or a third part, for if you empty more than that at once, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue tell the patient, and his pulses; then take out the instruments and retain the blood, and it is retained now by the spur which stamps the hole which is on the facet, as I have said, that you pierce according to this method; then repeat the instruments the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and give him a small quantity of blood. Do this for neither the first nor the second time until it no longer remains but a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If thou doubtest of the patient, and thou seest him emit drops of blood, if the cure of the sepulture or sand cautery, and by drops of sweat or bath and sun, and dost abstain from food; and dost administer dry medicines until he is cured, and cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the extraction of the blood, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the belly of the limb.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark in the belly, or the mark is small, or it is not well placed in its place
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the physician persists too long that he cannot perceive all the humors very subtle according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or prick the subtle humors of the bladder, and bind and hold them for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if he keeps the bladder closed, and he urinates, and then he can be set free; for by chance it cannot be closed, because the urine that comes out forces it open.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the cause of the opening is slight, if it is treated with a poultice, as we have said, if it swells.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening inside their limb are pale, for none are born with the opening at the root of the limb, for they cannot urinate before they elevate their limb high; and they cannot endure this because the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, then stretch out the head of the shoulder and the arm as wide as a pen, if the navel is pierced in the middle, as it should be; and hold back the discharge of blood that comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this blood is seen, cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils appear on the verge, and are a sign of foul matter; and there are both malignant and benign ones. If you wish to remove them, you must first apply a subtle ointment, then lance and crush them all, then apply a soaked cotton swab in Egyptian order; then bind with a diafinicon until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the swelling is malignant, dark and purulent, it is necessary that you apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the swelling is at the root of the limb, and has some in the belly and some outside, it is necessary that you reduce the swelling which is inside first; and when it is reduced, if the cure is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure the whole [wound], if it is not firmly held in place, the head of the shoulder will be perceived [as dislocated]; black bile and corruption will ensue in his head or shoulder; if you can remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and sometimes, cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes away, if you mix lunar cautery with this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two positions together: that is, at the discharge of blood, and at corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you swallow or induce vomiting, the patient will urinate; and when the hair has fallen out at the root of the beard which has not been shaved, or if there is wound or incision, if you can then singe it with the instrument that chews, as long as the tendons are loosened, and deliver the head of the shoulder from all parts; and if this is burdensome, if you can then touch it with the thumb and index finger of the other hand, then smear gently between them, and put on a bandage of fine linen moistened with cold water, which will not move away from its place.</start_of_turn>
de la circoncision	from the circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other wounds; although when we make this work of our own free will, and do it properly, if we make it better, it is the lightest in health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old ones did not speak of circumcision in their laws, because they did not use it in their customs, and we have only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who made circumcision around here, with force and all their skill; but when the urine escaped through the pores because there were two holes, and by chance if we cut off these above and left those below, the patient fled.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and the pain is doubled, and at the movement which is done too roughly, the point of the limb is not securely held; and by the movement of the bone by chance escapes the needle, and repairs the work, and many times they are born again without having had to move them and I desire it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the movement which is made there is force throughout the whole thread that I have proved to be beneficial in the experiment, for the forces tear just as well from above as from below.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equally taut in all directions, but the thread is well stretched around the skin; and if the movement is slight at first, as if you were reminding a child, if he understands, do not force him to tighten the thread too much around the limb, but simply bind it loosely around the limb; then make it firm between your hands or pull out the nails that the fetus cannot see, neither any of the instruments; then put your hand on the limb and sigh or groan, and draw it up as high as the head of the limb is elongated; then thoroughly cleanse the area that is collected, then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie it loosely from one end to the other; and hold for two turns at the pouch and the index finger, and hold between the two threads, then withdraw the groan from the fetus and draw out the head of the limb; then leave the blood to flow freely, as it is proper; and sprinkle with powder and on the powder a bandage glued with a piece of egg yolk boiled in rose water, confirmed with rose oil and rosemary, and leave it on until the other cure is complete.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the circumcision is thus: the two thumbs are tense and extended, and the fingers are as great as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The pain of the mundane if it comes from the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your fingernail, even if the wound makes a postscript; and hold it equally, and if you do not wish to hold it at your fingernail, if you hold it with your teeth, and then hold it.</p>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant. Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.
