dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The urine is retained if the stone, or blood congealed, or bile, or purulent matter, or other things which we have mentioned in the division, are present; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the stone is in the navel or the neck of the bladder, if it is possible that the patient is bent over his knees; and that they put their feet on the back, and extend their belly from the part under their back, and restrain the patient as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is desliie; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible that you administer an extraction with all the instruments which are called "siringues", in which this is the form: either of silver hammered out like a sparrow's beak; or the caine of a palm of long and a half; or hammered out.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the manner of extracting urine is such that you take two threads and bind one to the head of the bladder or of cloth, and pass the thread through the bladder; and drain the excess of cloth and pass until you reach the head of the bladder, then join the bladder with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the edge of the bed, and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moist and oily with olive oil and urine; then put the bladder steadily into the testicle as far as it reaches the root of the testicle, then double the testicle downwards towards the buttock; then withdraw the bladder again until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty, and this must not be done except in the case that the urine is leading or going in a different direction. Then draw the threads all the way out, and the urine follows the thread, then withdraw the thread, and correct the urine; and repeat the bladder until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When urine or blood comes into the bladder, or when pus is assembled there, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped by whom the doctor commands, so that he stamps well the limb with addition, if we can manage to remove the moisture, and push as much as necessary; and when you see the medicines dripping from the bladder, put the chief surgeon in the moisture, and drive out the one who is in front; if you drive out the moisture from the surgeon, and then push strongly the one in front; if the moisture enters the surgeon, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped by whom the doctor commands, so that he stamps well the limb with addition, if we can manage to remove the moisture, and push as much as necessary; and when you see the medicines dripping from the bladder, put the chief surgeon in the moisture, and drive out the one who is in front; if you drive out the moisture from the surgeon, and then push strongly the one in front; if the moisture enters the surgeon, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if this is the case; or of silver or gold, and the shoulder is higher; and two veins are swollen at the breast or the armpit; then take a bladder of a goat and put the moisture which you see clustering the bladder inside it, and tie between the two breasts a strong double thread, and burn one of those moistures on the fire; then bring back the chief of the cluster to the limb, and strain your hand over the bladder with all the moisture that comes out, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round about the edges; then pass the thread strongly through these holes, and assemble the circle as though you were assembling a doll, and put inside it what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it up with the instrument; and do as though you had made the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes out of the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the preceding parts the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction with medicines; and we mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that is not, and the signs of each. In what case should we perform an incision for a stone? In the bladder and the kidney; and I shall tell you openly and concisely.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone which is retained in the bladder is often the cause of vomiting, and this is a sign that the bladder is greatly irritated throughout its substance; there is open hazing, and the patient feels great pain in the belly and has many vomiting spells, and then grows pale; and from these vomiting spells the foundation is loosened; and it is light for the patient to recover from vomiting until the age of three, and is much more difficult in the elderly, and is like that in young people and old people; and the cure for the large stone is easier than for the small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first purify the patient by vomiting, to bring out all the evil that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never happens that we are able to explore the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of one side of the bone and the other above, then draw the limb over the bone between the two joints, and then extract it forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if it is true, when you feel the knee bones are out of place you will know it.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if it does not go away, if you put a piece of broken glass on the wound and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the knee is strong, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting the arrow from its home will help you in your work; and if it does not go away, and if it is a vein that has been cut, if you put powder on the wound and bind it tightly with bands, and do not attempt to move it again, and leave the knee alone, except in an emergency where the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the color of blood has subsided and the limb is relaxed, if you return to your work while the wound is still open, as long as the wound is still bleeding.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as the kernels of corn, that contains the yolk; and it is called "syfac," and never is it properly within the yolk, if we take care that it is not otherwise. And it is the skin of the kernel between the white fat that we have said. And these do not move together.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramus is from weakness and comes from the kernels, and the matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes upon the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either a pale yellow, or without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are signs of corruption of this assembly, for if it is pale yellow or white as we have said, if the abscess is reinous, I would say long as a sausage, and it does not open the joints, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is reinous with a portion of the yolk, and because of this it is thought that it is another sausage; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white substance, if one feels well; then when you know the color of the moisture, if you see that it is throughout, from which it appears that the shape is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which follows the introductor, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we licure by fire, if it is commanded that the patient be sound as before and the restoration of his limb; then we bind him upon his back, upon something high, and put under him a bundle of cloths; then we sit upon his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the arm up to one of the two ribs which are two fingers distant from the navel; then we take the sponge soaked in liquid, and we cut the skin of the ribs among the bones up to the navel; and we make our incision straight, dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white fascia; and we burn it secretly as before; then we pierce the fascia with a needle at one large hole, and we drain all the fluid, and then we put in our sponges, and withdraw the needle; and do not touch the bone of the ribs, but only the fascia; cut off all or in pieces immediately the cost of it secretly, for if you do not cut it well, the fluid will return; and if the urine spurts from your work, if you leave it in its place when you have completed the work of the fascia.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the abscess corrupted by another disease, then you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then cut through the abscess thoroughly, drain the pus, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is gathered in two parts together, like two branches; if you press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound a piece of clean linen soaked in oil of roses; and put upon it another layer of linen soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two nails, and put under doubled cloths, and bind it up as it is said above.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool thread as said above and assemble them by stitching in the armpit; and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the shoulder, and the other at the side of the shoulder; and the other two nails on the two angles, and assemble everything so that the restriction is in the loop of the armpit; and never is this branch of cautery treated with the size of a sword, and only take one surgical cautery, and press the skin of the nails, and if as we have said, if the white spot that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the cautery as said above, and pierce that spot as we have uncrossed, and burn it with this subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And look at all the ways you can, until you are done; and keep that the fire does not touch the yolk; and save that this work is more salve; and move that you keep the incisions of blood, and more delicate than the works of size; and if anything hinders you, or incisions or other things, if you can cure what hinders you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if he suspects perforation, as I have said, and as soon as you are certain by the meanings we have said that the aquous solution is lying, if you make the patient sit on a low seat; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with all the surrounding area wide, and make the perforation long and thin; and if the wound is large, so that all the blood flows out; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and leave to drain the remaining blood, and cure until the wound is healed; and if the white bile does not allow the blood to drain from the wound, as you must drink a penny or the instrument with which the blood is treated from the hydrophics, because it is like this; and enlarge the wound, and save that the blood returns, and reassemble after six months or when the wound is healed, and when it is reassembled as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The hairs that are in the root of this limb are numerous and cause fear in many; for I believe that their value is not in leaving them; and I shall tell you the work and the resemblance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, when the abscess comes or bursts, and there are stitches; and this is often the case
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive rubbing and swelling, which is spread over the bones, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess is like that of fresh blood; and there is no pain, and it is painful; and by chance it is one abscess that is grasped, painful and bloody, and of a dark colour, and never comes from any artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the position of the abscess, when you press it with your thumb; and it must not be touched by you
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his arrangement at the expression of pain in the thighs, and can well make the size upon this semblance, and upon the other limbs; and is that you press like a key against the coions, then the egg is up, and the thread is from white silk, and delivers the yolk from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soiled with these limbs, if you can then only draw the egg and press; and if it is at the silk or in the blood vessels, if you can deliver all that is thick, and press round
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if it is towards the socket, or within the blood vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and round off the edges.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, if you apply a bandage of coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the coions, and the patient groans greatly when he goes; and the cure for this disease is well known as before, and all that we can say about it is what the ancient ones did
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on the left side of the chair, and then hold the suspension of the collarbones to his chest, to all the vessels that are below the ribcage, and grasp them firmly, and extend them outwards; then pierce with a needle through the tough tissue between the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then drain from the front, as we said in the extraction of the arteries from the temples; then insert a needle or there is a double thread, and tie it to the first loop or the knot has come loose, and tie it to the other end; then close tightly around the middle, according to the length of the hair, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as usual or apply a bandage, so that no vessel is cut other than those which naturally bleed from the collarbones; for in this case there will be no harm, and if all the vessels are cut, it is better to remove the collarbones from all the vessels; if he does not lose his nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they are dry and do not bleed further.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dries and does not yield aid.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The event of this branch is by section which comes or syfac, or extension on the belly in the part of the spleen, for which the intestine descends from that route to one of the coils; and this route is either the syfac or the extension of the latter, and comes from these two modes of motion: by percussion, or jump, or pressure, or the raising of grief faix, and by similar things; and the sign that this is the extension of the syfac is that there is a pause and a pause, in long tension, and does not come immediately; and the apostemes are equal until towards the navel, for that the syfac presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it suddenly causes pain in the ear, and the swelling is different from the normal, with the skin taut and pale, because of the escape of the intestine and the swelling of the jaw.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never do the bones move with the intestine, and is retained when forced, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when pressed.</start_of_turn>
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these fiery cures with fear, for fear itself suffices.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient instructs that the intestine be held in the hand towards the depth of the wound if it can enter; then either saw above the collar between the hands, and hold the thighs; then stretch the thumb over the top, and cut all the skin of the coils along; then push inwards the leaves of the size of an almond according to what you must master to open the wound, and so that these are the same as those that make it impossible for it to go further; then stretch the syfac that is outside the skin of the coils, as long as the thick syfac is discovered from all sides; then put your index finger in that which teaches the coil, in that which is between the white syfac which is outside the skin of the egg, and between the second syfac, and depart that which is behind the egg, and between the second syfac; and because it moves the hand of the side of the coil, and put the white syfac at the top of your left hand, and hold the egg towards all the syfac towards the size; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and unhook that which is behind the ligament; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or white syfac hardened, and if you find nothing, if it is at the bottom of the wound; then take a needle or there is a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the coils; after the size, then cut the ends that appear from the threads, until there are three threads; and assemble them one on the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the syfac, of which we have said that it is outside the skin of the coils, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the ends of the threads, and bind them in two parts, so that no vessels which support them can enter inside, except for the wound that remains; and remove the thread according to the first thread along two fingers of that, and after these two threads leave the syfac that is outside the coil the greatest of a finger; and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is outside the skin of the coils, as much as it is without repair, and bend it over, as we have said before; then apply coarse wool soaked in oil, and put in the wound, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	Never cauterize the flesh except as I have said after the incision, in doubt of bloodletting
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood, and leaving the vein open until it bleeds; and if it delays at the root, if it arises from a hot wound, put on what we have said, until it bleeds; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this limb I have never seen anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made just like the twig which joins the nut, in part like that you bind the veins, after the size above loosely to the outside; then press inward, and cure the abscess of that which causes it, until the veins bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes rupture among the angry ones, as we have said, and open the eyes; and do not feel any intestines as stones, and if there are, that is enough, and repair them all the hours; and all of them if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or the swelling, until the intestines come out; and this comes from the stretching of the sinew which is angry, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflamed the eyes and open; and cure it if by cautery, as we have said before; and never cured by iron in this manner: and that the patient lies soundly on his back between your hands, then press the eye of the rupture swells with the large of three two; and then remove the swelling that is from the outside of the leather that covers it, then take the thread and bring out the eye appearing from the swelling; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut out the two eyes appearing from the swelling on the top of the thread, and cut one and the other; then remove the head of the thread, and do not cover the swelling or extend the yolk of anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines; then cure by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you have closed the wound, if the swelling and cure the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no apparent cause in the course of treatment, and the cautery is mute in this limb, and more proximate to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the nails becomes soft in old age, because the nails themselves are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when it is seen to be cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to remove the soft skin from the natural skin; then join the two layers together with a suture, and if you see that, leave the excess of soft skin at two or three sutures; then close between the sutures, and cure as with the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement,
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	The wounds which are scraped off in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force them except for two cases: the first is that the witness to the wound responds when asked, and the cure of the wound; and the second, because we often see best friends of ours being forced to swear by their attendants, as with oxen and sheep and cats and other beasts.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that swearing is done in two ways: by attraction, or by incision.</start_of_turn
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, we make the best sit in hot water, until the joint is softened and flexible; then we grasp it with our hand, until it is set and you no longer feel it.</start_of_turn
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the limb's fracture: command that you hold it firmly, and press the skin of the nails on your left hand, then bind the suspension; and place a bandage over each wound as many times as necessary until you have firmly secured them; and leave no wound open or any hidden wound which is outside the blood vessels; and this method of treatment is milder than that which is done by traction, because traction leaves no trace of the nails, for which reason it desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways as follows: one if between the two nails appears as the figure of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes it emits urine in the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other kind is in women, and has on the navel as a beard and two nails.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for boils and carbuncles is that you lance the boils open all, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for those whose urine spurts through the pores of the buttocks, if there is no other cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways: one if between the two testicles is open as in the figure of nature in a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine is held back. And the other way if in women, and has on the navel as a beard and two testicles. And the cure for the swelling and fame is if you crush the testicles completely, and the cure is like for other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tinder is a boil on the natural part [of the body], as long as it is too painful to see; and many women have it as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you keep the superfluousness of the tinder at your hand or armpit, and grasp it lightly; and do not go too deeply, for there is risk of bleeding, and that is what causes death; and there is another disease that arises at the mouth of the marris, and the swelling, and by chance spurts out, and is similar to a cow’s foot, and for this reason it is called the ancient “plague of the cow”.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you have grasped it, as we have said, hold the limb steady until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the nature of the woman is not clearly perceived, or if the wound is small; and it is natural by birth, or due to an accident of illness that comes with it; or it is caused by a sudden injury, or by a swelling or scab, and is made by a wound in the marrow, or in the cost, or in the eyes, or in any other place; and if it breaks the conception, and the birth, and by chance the flowers have come to have; and the knowledge of this is by the attention of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling appears close to the surface, if you desire to the two or to the root
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a swelling of the spleen that is close to the surface, if you are in a hurry, and the spleen is ruptured; put your two index fingers together, and the patient should lie on their back, with their legs spread; then the two levers are formed, as long as the spleen is round, and is over the swelling; then take oil, and soak the wound in it, and put it on the limb, and hold the patient still, until the swelling subsides.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, as you must keep it from pressing against the cartilage resembling a ivy leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling is of cartilage, if you suspend it at the navel and keep it pressed; and have medicines that are staying in place, such as chamomile, dragon’s blood, incense, and plenty of egg; then mix in a dose of lead plaster, so that the wound cannot heal; and keep it long, and mix in some lint of flaxseed; then be cured of other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there comes swelling of cartilage, if you cover it as described above, this will prevent abscesses from forming.</start_of_turn>
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the swelling of cartilage that is in the marrow, do not touch it with fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	From boils.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are openings of veins which without support customarily, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become thick; and as we have said in the preceding parts, their signs and symptoms I will say here those which resolve the cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thick ones, when they are pressed down into the marrow, and are not felt, if not by the iron cure
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the armpit steady, grasp it by the root, then sprinkle some restraining medicines around it, such as chamomile and dragons blood and incense, and similar things; then bind its parts for an hour, then put it in cold water; and when it softens, remove the dressing. If blood comes, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and mustard, and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sticks, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make a ventouse on the back and apply butter; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with old wine, and apply it to the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the abscess has healed, if the wound has bled so much as to be healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a black head, if you cover it so as I have said before; and then heal the wound when it is healed.</start_of_turn
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without support are usually not cured; and when they are old they become thick; and we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those which bring about healing. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow and are not perceived, can only be cured by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow can be perceived, and can be cured. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then strengthen the ankle and hold the shin bone in its roots, then sprinkle upon it medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close the wound an hour later, then bathe it in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and oatmeal, and make one application on her back. And if it stops bleeding, that is good. If not, if there is still bleeding, make her breathe with a cloth over her back and apply pressure; then take linen, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her breathe. And when the wound has healed, if it is not completely cured, it will become white like a rough chief; if you cover it as I have said the thick blood. And then it will be cured when it is completely healed.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many kinds of abscesses that come in the belly, such as carbuncles and purulent abscesses and herpes and piles and tumors and fistula and hemorrhoids and chautier abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is commanded that when the cautery is applied to the boil which appears in the marrow, which is not a simple boil but which collects pus; if you know the work of iron, look whether the boil is already in the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not immediately pierce, but let me measure until the pain is calmed; then seat the patient on a chair and make two small stools or he will slump, and support him on his back and bring his limbs close to his body; let his thighs be spread wide, and place his knees against his groin, and bind them well with a linen bandage; then draw out the swelling towards the breastbone, and bring the instrument which we use to open the marrow, so that this is the shape; and know that when you bring this instrument, first feel the depth of the marrow, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the marrow with a drape, so that the instrument does not grieve; and command that he put on the horn of the instrument at the base, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when an abscess bursts, and we wash the hand with the palm facing inwards, if the thumb covers the chief, at the wrist; and when the wound is empty, if you put in the wound some soft materials in olive oil rose or dry green oil; put the dressing firmly over the wound and put over it a bandage of linen net soaked in vinegar or mallow, which must be cooked; then cure after two days of washing following this, until it is healed. And under no circumstances lift the dressing and the wound with a clamp of water and honey, and then water or licorice root and elderberry long must be cooked; then resume the washing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound has healed in the wound cavity, if you must guard against burning, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From infancy
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first teaches that she who knows the figure of natural infancy shall recognize the signs when a woman presses down on the navel and desires to smell the navel-cord; then she must immediately deliver the child; for when the navel descends on the head, the second stage follows her, and the belly swells with her; and when these signs are seen, if she presses gently on her belly, the child will be delivered head first; for when he descends on the head, she follows him, and the mistress delivers the afterbirth by natural force.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never happens by chance that the limbs or the head, or the hands, or any part descends; or that the belly swells or contracts, or that it hangs limp and is converted by accident from its collar, and by other harmful figures; if the mistress is skilled in the art, she will be wise and discreet in these matters, and will avoid error and deception, and I will show her all the figures which she must employ in order to aid her.</start_of_turn>
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out naturally from the head and the woman gives birth and the strength of the child is weak, if you make her sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and when she has relaxed with oil or rue or fennel, which is customary, then you should hold the child between your two arms and gently push the little heel that gives it its shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and bind its nail until the moisture which is in its core is consumed; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clench the woman with the muscle of fenugrec with oil of sisament; then make her take in and expel a concoction, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if it is now expelled.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out violently, then it is necessary that you hold them lightly back and forward; and if they do not enter, put the woman on a seat, and support her feet high up; then pull the seat away from the earth, and hold the woman, that she does not cough; and if the hands do not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you press the hands to the breastbone which is above mentioned, and pull out the fetus, and make it equal.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on his feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on his feet, if you can push upwards; then bend his leg forward and backward, until they are even; then grasp the toes and stretch them forward and backward.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps up to his buttocks, if the master commands him to grasp, and makes him cough out of his chest; if he jumps too high, God help him.</start_of_turn
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not forced as we have said, if the joint hangs too low or too high, as long as it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is easily displaced.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump up so eagerly as we have commanded, say that he should take muscle laxatives, oil of poppies, gum masticatory, and broth; and mix all in a mortar; and put over the woman's belly and drive away this vomiting, then make her sit in cold water until the ribs are numb; and when she is softened up from the cold, give her a collar of myrrh, and put on her clothes, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on her seat, then make her vomit and strain her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly gently, for the child now jumps.</start_of_turn
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the child’s discharge from his genitals.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands on his shoulders and his head down; then either he is overcome with nausea on his collar, and hangs his head down; or he lets out a fart and looks away; he folds his hands on his chest and then grasps the hands on his belly, and pulls the cushions of his buttocks towards the navel, until it is visible in the mouth; and if the child does not jump, take his hands and move them forward, then move his hands up to his belly, and he will let out a fart; and he will be still and quiet; and command the woman to stay until the child is better.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	and the boy cries out loud; and instructs the woman to look after him until the boy is well.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you to restore the limb: if you are unable to restore it, if you make the woman rise up and call for help; if she is unable to call for help, if you make her lie down and put the legs forward; then bring in the muscle I mentioned before. And if she does not recover, if you make her sit on the chair, then study to restore the limb; and when the limb is restored, according to the natural shape, make her expectorate, and command her to stay until the child is better.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child on his neck, and his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command thee that thou graspest her hand firmly, then turn it back and forward, and move it lightly; and when it is even, apply the caustic substance of alum and oil, as we have said before; then command her to move it back and forth; and when thou hast done this, cause her to sit upon a chair and command her to lean forward; and she shall vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same manner at all the second time.

These instruments are all very strong, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when you behold them appear, the work hastens and the houses are higher in quantity.

de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodulations, and those that come from below the foundation are more serious, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when the nodulation is old, if it is renewed, and is accompanied by moisture or white spots or bumps, these fistulas are never cured; and they are known by the fact that there is stool or vomiting or diarrhea when the patient defecates, or by chance when one leaps.</start_of_turn
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach as far as the hip joint, and even to the bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows of the fistula persisting at the base, and not leaving: and it is only that you bite your thumb index or base, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no torsion.

And if there is torsion, if you insert a slight attempt of a sponge or horsehair, as long as you feel the attempt or the hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no risk of bleeding, vomiting, or discomfort, as we have said: such as that which does not pierce me; if you hurry to cure.</start_of_turn>

If it is pierced up to the hip joint, if there is a vein attempt up to the root; if there is no torsion and the invention of pain there, if it is that it is already bowed down, and there is no medicine or support by oil; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except toil, and the worthlessness of silly people who get in the way.</start_of_turn>
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that one which is neither new nor old, hope of health lies by fire, as I have seen; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and that you support the legs until above his knees, and that you incline his knees towards his belly; then attempt to draw out the splinter or plunge if there is discomfort, until you have extracted it or the attempt comes.

If the patient feels pain at the root, if you must bite down your thumb, if he then feels that the attempt has been perceived; or if the thumb or the index finger is broken, then extract the splinter which is present; if not, it will not be healed.

One can easily heal all sorts of things, but this is not so; and what helps in this is to burn the cautery cautiously according to the size of the fistula, as it is said; and pour toutes les autres choses, keep the wound covered with a dressing until the root is gone; and do this twice or thrice, until you are certain that these worms which are like the bristles of an oyster must be burned; and then cauterize the wound with smooth tentes and sew.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is truly healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is truly healthy, it is well; for if he attempts between, and does not pierce to the root which is or should be the foundation, and between your thumb and the attempt a thick covering of hair or chaff, and you see the fistula at that which the covering departs from; if the head of the fistula is grasped from the commencement of the fistula, and is held fast before the attempt, and is cauterized afterwards, until it comes to the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and cherished. Then praise those hairs that seem like a bundle of hair, and do not leave anything remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he does not go away of his own accord, and stands between you and the work, let the fire cautery or the medical potion suffice.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two bones: namely, the burning of these hairs that are around it, and the coagulation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wounds that are moist and soft in bran or chaff, until the liquid blood flows; and isse force the hairs to burn in the flow; then cure the wound of the wounds that are surrounded by soft hair, and the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	When the fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the bone or root is grasped or grasped at the root, ask for that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the urging, and between the second and the fourth rib, or the spleen or the liver, or if it be near to pierce, if there be no other remedy but flight and hope, by the administering of one of the three methods: either thou cauterize as we have said, or thou bind it until it is whole, or if thou wilt thou may take it with force and cure as first; and do not go too deep, that thou cover only that which holds the foundation, and let the discharge go in the natural order; then cure as we have said; by chance if it be well, or thou draw out that covering and the mud then when it is bound from the foundation, or by force or by other pointed instrument; then bind up that which is in the wound, as thou wilt; and study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the lower part of the foundation: if it be a less arduous thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas like this: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or is deeply rooted under the skin, if you take a bite pierced at the head like this.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thus .i. feel the thread twisted in two, and hold the attempt at all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And if it persists at the root of the foundation, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your root or foundation; and draw out the head of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and strain one against the other, and leave it hanging there for one or two; and do not restrain it ever, until the thread overcomes these burdens that are between two bones, and yields. Then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not break through, if you force it to break in every way you can, it will not be too deeply seated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to force it from the surrounding tissue if it is deeply seated, and then it will cure, as we have said, when it is sound.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny burdock from which we make the fistula is thick and hard at one end and soft and slippery at the other; and because of this we must not grasp this with our hands, as we see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
