Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorries are of two kinds: when they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are a few or many of them, and they are firm in blood; or when there is one or more of them, and they are soft or pale yellow or bloodstained, and have the color of wax. As for those which are deep in the foundation, if you command the patient to stretch and rise from bed, as long as the foundation is forced out, the thread will appear. If you are hasty and grasp his finger or nail, then grasp them at their roots; if they cannot be held by their moisture, then take hold of them with a bandage or lint or a piece of chammel, and pull them out, then grasp them, and powder over them hot powders which are in lieu of cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the treatise of cautery, for other cures are as effective when they are healthy. If the foundation cannot be forced out, if you bite the patient with a biting and abrasive clistere, it will force out what is in or under the foundation, so that it can be forced out openly. When the patient does not feel it and the thread is forced out of the foundation, if the cure is legitimate, grasp his finger or nail and grasp them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and that they fear the incision with the knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is certain that you have restored the shoulder according to this method: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through under and out, and twist two threads of the thread together, and if it is thick; strain the thread together, then knot the thread and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to hold the surplus of blood; then put on the foundation a bandage soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it heals, and when it is healed, if the wound has healed and other treatments, until it is whole.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	When the wound is dry or healed at its base.</start_of_turn>
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There is often a dry discharge of blood in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is certain that you have reduced a sprain or a dislocation of the nail at the base of the nail, which does not allow it to dry; then treat it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it cannot be healed, if you must renew the scraping more strongly than before, until the wound bursts, and is scraped away; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	because he is groaning.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance that grows before the body, and goes out like a mouse; and never does it leave the true without bruising, and one feels it as if dead from fear, and comes throughout the body, and more so than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure for this is to take a needle of goose feather or a strong needle of bull, and put that needle on the wound, until the circle turns purple around the wound; then pull the hand away from the needle as much as you can until you reach the wound, and pull it out, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see that it is done with a wasp or iron according to this form, and that the edges are blunt and the underside is rough:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you see that it is done with a wasp or iron according to this form, and that the edges are blunt and the underside is rough, do not be afraid, for it is necessary to hold tightly and press firmly. If you see that the fire is applied, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of this form.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is copper or silver cautery made, or of wasp or molten iron; and never are these small and great instruments made as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in their upbringing and in their treatment are petty.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a small and great blister is thus when it is surrounded by a wide area, or when the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is swelling or the belly is bound, if you see, and the shoulder is dislocated either forward or backward; and there are two punctures on one rib and one on the other; or if the belly or abdomen holds the medicines in a bladder of best or parchment, or if it is pierced throughout around the wounds, and there is one space between each puncture, then put in this puncture one strong thread of silk or cotton twisted like an X or around like a nail; and assemble the belly as though it were a hoop. And when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument before a strong thread, then clip; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold; rub the head of the blister with oil or the yolk of an egg, or something similar; then bind it loosely; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is quite swollen; then draw out the blister, and leave the patient’s legs exposed, and if the medicine wishes, if he can bear it; and if he sleeps all night, that is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it in a state of sickness of swelling of the belly, and the physician hasten to leave, if it starts again as long as it is sane.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling at the root or the base of the blister, if the blister is as subtle as for one child; that is the form of a subtle blister that is stretched over the skin:
des plaies	And thus it is with the form of a subtle blister on the skin that the leather is strained: from wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the preceding section the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and medicine, as it is completed.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to the way they are made, and according to the place or the wound is made, and of what material it is made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are biting of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or sickle, or similar things; or that are done according to the customs of the country, as for example a wound that bites on the neck, or on the head, or the elbow, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a superficial wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come to mind in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone wound or similar things, and the skin is thoroughly torn and the wound is large, you doubt the cause of the wound: if you do so immediately without delay, the head of the fracture will be better even if blood comes from the wound; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the wound; and listen to the patient’s complaint of a full stomach and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, if either vomiting blood or eating does not cease, do not eat meat or drink wine; and remove the wound, if there is suspicion of an abscess; smear clotted ointment in oil rose only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no suspicion of an abscess, put a cover on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, or anything else, I will tell you later; and if it has been moved, put on some dressings, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as if made by a sword and similar things, and the edges do not come together by tension, if you join them with sutures, as I will say, for wounds of the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by the bone, and is raw, and can only be held together by a staple, then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as meat and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or leather putrefying, and it does not touch the bone, if you staple it all, and pour in urine, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if you can, and if you find it dislocated, if you bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, if you cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, if it is a mild cure: and if you put on this powder that adheres as soon as it moves.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them finely, and apply to the wound, and bind firmly, until it is well healed and reunited with all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for we do not put medicine on a wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Never do we make this burn only, when we do not have incense or dragon’s blood, but that the wound has not moved.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved from its original position, even while at rest, do not apply any ointment; but put upon some absorbent materials, or poultices of ground barley made with water and honey, until it has dried; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, if you grasp the wound with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about fractures later.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	Wound comes from the collar and it is simple, if there is no difference between the neck and the chest, but if the neck or the artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the nerve is affected, if there is no other remedy than leaving the wound open, and do not put any restrictive dressing, because it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of the disease is with the brain, which is the most sensitive limb; but if the disease is severe, like a boiled egg in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and chamomile boiled in sweet water, and other stones of the earth according to this method, and moist dressings.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, if the pain and swelling persist, then the treatment must be continued until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and full of blood, if the artery is severed, or there is discharge of blood from the wound, or the caulking or cauterizing has not been done correctly; if the thorn of the throat is severed, or the cord is cut, and the tongue is held back by force, because the meat hangs down on the cord of the throat; then the head should be strained immediately, and left in that position for some days; then the wound should be treated with ointment until it is healed; if the wound has caused an indentation in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments must be pulled out, these must be left out as long as the wound persists; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, do as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of wound from spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if thou seest that the wound is of such force that the patient cannot support himself; then shalt thou take out the arrow immediately; for if it be not deep, and it be fresh throughout its extent, if thou dost not put in at the first hour the powder, thou shalt not bind it up with the dressing only when it is sore and deep; but thou shalt remove it from the wound and comfort the patient; but thou shalt put in a effectual astringent, and bind it twice round; and if thou dost not have an astringent, thou shalt put into the wound fine cotton to absorb the moisture, and shalt make the patient lie upon the wound for three days, or four, or more; for if it does not yield to this, do not move or strain the limb, nor give him any nourishment. When thou seest the bones displaced, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tension of the tendons and other cures, as long as he is sane; and if it cannot heal, and if there is pus, drain the abscess that has formed; if the cure is like this.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or a knife, and it is simple or deep, front or back, if the treatment for what is before; if it is large, suture; if it is small, powder; and if it is stuck in the bone, and pieces have broken off, if you wish for the wound, and the surrounding tissue has been damaged; and if it has not been damaged, if you leave it alone, if it aligns with the extractions; and for other wounds, as for other members, the judge will decide as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The belly has been dislocated.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The swelling of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound no time the intestines do not go out, or do not touch the intestines, because of the introduction of pus; and the suture is more painful, and no time is better than the little wound than the great, because for this we can put the intestines back one by one; for as the intestines expand so that they feel the fruit, if they go back in one by one, and for this reason is better the lesser wound, because we can keep the intestines in their place like others. And abscesses that rupture from the belly are in three ways: the two common costures come in the costure of the belly, and the costure of the other wounds of bone and two other costures are common to other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the costure of the belly, and I will say one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and only a little thing is pressing, this can be remedied in two ways: either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are distended by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, bathe it in part with oil: moisten a sponge or I will drape it in warm water only, or you will burn in warm vinegar and resin and prick, and rise the intestine as long as it is swollen; and do not do this movement too tightly, and be quiet that we may avoid bursting
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if moisten the intestine with water or if cooked meat and blood are cooked, for by this is the opening of the entrance to many things; and if it cannot enter, if make a hole in the wound at the instrument to grasp the blood clots; and the first treatment is quiet that the size is not made greater than necessary, and it is the instrument for cutting: if it is cut inwards in the curve and does not slip out, and once this is done, cut in this fashion:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude forward, if you stop bleeding according to the natural shape in its own place, you will have done well, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put his head and arm higher than the lower parts, and in the same way if the swelling is in the upper part of the belly, put the lower part and the hand higher than the upper part; and thus you must bring to an end what I have said concerning great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, put what has appeared between your hands, and put a bandage that embraces all the swelling; and this is the common way of stitching, and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound, then leave some space at the head of the wound, and pierce the two holes in the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is through the skin inwards, until you have pierced through that part, and assemble the two heads of the needle together; then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, and assemble the two edges of the wound together, and then leave some space, and pierce another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing this until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles catch all the flesh, and the thick ones do not penetrate well: for this reason they should be neither too fine nor too thick; and do not push the needles too far from the flesh and the skin, for they catch and open the wound before the suture; and then trim the ends of the needles, that they do not irritate the patient at sleep, and put patches or dressings over the holes of the needles in order to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only need for one or two needles for the second stitching, and that you assemble the two holes in the skin and the two holes in the needle together with one needle or with a strong thread in the middle; and when you have pierced these holes all together, remember the needle at the part where you began, in the manner in which you cut the threads; and leave some space between each stitch the thickness of a small fist; this stitch is suitable for a home, and I stitched a wound once on a hip or belly, which was caused by a knife, and the wound was more than half an inch wide, and there were intestines well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I shall return the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound has been closed for fifteen days; the cure was applied, and it has healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he saw that it was dead, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with any medicine, for I was in Italy where there was no medicine, no remedies; and I did nothing more on the wound than twice daily dressing it with wool, and applying honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it through from the underside until it reaches the midpoint; when it has grasped the right corner to the right, if the skin slips or tears or if you have passed the needle, and you make it pierce from the other side of the underside until it reaches the edge; and you understand this stitching if you sew like a leatherworker and leave once the slip of one side, and take it back from the other, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens describes as proper, is as follows: if two parts are naturally joined together, and one of the ends is applied to the other at the midpoint: pierce a needle or the nearby end, and pierce only the lower part, leaving the two ends of the former intact; then withdraw the needle, and pierce from the lower part until it reaches the middle, leaving two ends; then pierce the one and the other from the lower part until they reach the middle, in two other holes made on the opposite side; and this is the most perfect and common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says concerning this passage, and no one contradicts him, that the belly must be sewn with two needles, or there must be yarn in the bobbin; and one needle must be fastened at one end and the other at the other, in the manner of those who sew coarse cloth. And so it is that when the wound has receded somewhat from the belly, if the stitching is finer than usual, it will be better
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the cost, then put on the healing powder; if it has moved, do not put on any dressing except for what is present, until the wound has healed; and close the wound, and join the edges, and the edges of the wound; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed. If you have no medicines, if put on, as soon as it begins to ooze blood, wool felt, and move it twice the time until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine for most wounds except in principal limbs; and if you doubt that the wound does not make common cause with the principal parts, you must cover it with coarse linen soaked in warm olive oil or rose oil, and put it on the wound, and drain the abscesses; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and this often happens, if you give it clusters of black wine, and even if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines; and pierce through, and drain what is inside, as when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called 'jeuns' cannot heal when they are swollen, for it is by the swelling of the veins that they are, and by the subtlety of the whole body, and by the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the wound spurts blood, if you put it back as before when the intestine is fresh; and if it is old and becomes black or dark, if you tie the black part, do not fear that blood will come, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the bone, and hang the two thumbs down from the part below the wound until the blood has clotted, to align the extraction when the blood spurts out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	De la routure dou boueil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in the abdomen, because I have seen that one bone was swollen or wounded by a spear; and the wound was at the stomach's side, and it became filled and turned into a fistula, and in that there was egestion and vomiting; I cured it according to that which I could, and I did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the wound closed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	When I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has anything wrong in his belly; but there is no point of harm, but a great many favorable dispositions, and food and drink; and they say that whenever there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be closed in parts. Take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have grasped the opening, if you place two fingers above the opening, so that it is strained, and then close the wound, and this is kept until it cannot be undone; then put in another tweezers like before, until the wound is entirely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief [of the intestines] tears in the intestines, and there is no other nuisance to the patient, and it can be closed with a fine thread that is cut from the intestines of a beast, in parts. Take the head of this thread of intestine that is already detached, and then join to the head of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted, and pass the thread through the needle, and close the intestine, and keep it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce except according to the way of fashion and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no other ailment, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	From fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and abscesses, when they burst, are universally called "fistules," and indeed when they are chewed and come to a boil.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is indeed a nodulation that must be durable and white, for there is neither pain nor swelling; and it is as much chewed as the quill of a bird; sometimes it bursts clearly and sometimes thickly; sometimes not at all, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, is only fierce by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or the bone; or by its malice; or because there is a hard pus inside, and on the face, that does not allow pus to grow; or there is too much swelling; or the blood vessels are hardened, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is excessive due to pestilence; or because the property of the region is tardy in digestion and in health, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone: and I have already mentioned all these causes and their signs and cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or I must tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by an egg of the hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that arise in all limbs due to infection; for there are wounds which arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the joint, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or on some of the bones, or on the backbone, or on any joint of the hands or feet; and if a part comes to the property of the main limb, and the rest.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the fistulas of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no fistula which does not reach the marrow except as I have said, and you have undertaken to cure it, and you see it approaching, if it is straight, if the marrow is soft; and if it is crooked, if you can plunge a needle so as to break the curvature, for the marrow is softened by the heat of the fistula; and if the fistula is wide open and you do not wish to seal it by stitches, if you can clench one of the edges by the other, for the moisture is short from one edge to the other, and the surrounding tissue is softened; then you must know if there is bone or nerve, and if there is swelling around the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any other part which I have mentioned, if the swelling is as I have said, and the bone is fractured, and the char is corrupted which is within; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted on the right side, if you can clench it firmly, as much as you wish; then put poultices soft and moist in medicine, and keep them until the medicine has eaten away the superfluous matter which remains at the bottom; and then put on oily unguents to the wound, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is fractured by the fistula, if it is grasped.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve is not swollen or the principal limbs are not affected, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered to be fractured, and there is corruption and blackness, if the marrow is whole as long as the corruption is bone-like, then cure the thing cautiously as long as it is sane; and if it is not sane, and rent bowe as before, extract the bone fragments until you reach the marrow; if you discover it and desire to do so as long as you are at the bottom, extract the whole corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is once again sane, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that is not the case, extract the fragments of corruption that are too deep; do not attempt to do anything further; if there is nothing else to be done except to leave it to nature; and if there is only a small bone fractured, and you wish to treat it, do so cautiously with pliers; if the extraction is done with a suitable instrument and there is no other bone, do not leave even a fragment; and if moisture opposes you, and there is neither doubt nor fear, grasp and moisten and draw out the bone fragments.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If thou dost not wish to remove them at an hour, put upon the wound some substance that hinders corruption, and leave them until the wound is completely healed over the bones; then it will be easier to remove them. If it is a large bone, as a limb or thigh, reduce the corruption as much as possible until the bone is whole again, and then restore the wound. If there be much corruption and the bone comes out to the surface, cover it with silk and cover all until the corruption has ceased; then cure the wound until it is healed. I tell thee of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that thou may take example and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years of age who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the bone, so that the matter went up to the leg, and he bled from a large abscess, but there was no apparent cause for the abscess; but they put it down to madness and they opened it so much that they corrupted a great deal of matter, and there became a fistula, and there came out a lot of pus that flowed and moistened the bone; and they continued to treat him for two years, but there was no skill in their hands, as far as I know, until I left there, and I saw his leg and the medicines they gave him, and what cured him of the fistula, which was the great swelling of the bone; and the bone became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I made an attempt in one of these holes, and then circled all the holes, and found that one followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I was hasty then, and I cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found corrupted and rotten, and it extended to the marrow; I cured the corruption that I saw of the rotten bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I saw; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but I could not fix it; and then I began again, and I discovered the bone just as before, and I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I cured it, and then I left it, and I thought I had fixed the limb; but I could only do that as long as I held a palm of the bone, and the marrow was thrown out whole, and then I restored it with medicines; and it healed and was firm, and did not swell any more, except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had to avoid for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is blood evacuated thus, but he remained whole; and from his bone there sprung a hard scale, and was in good condition and did not suffer any hindrance or discomfort at any time, neither in eating nor in walking.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no place but at the bonehead, if you must bind it in this manner: take one thread and stretch it to the top of the bone that breaks, and command no one to pull it out; and put another thread of linen thicker than the first, and bind it on the scale that is above the bone, and stretch the top, so that you tear out the corrupt scale, and uncover the scale above the bone where you see it bound; and put on a bandage or a sponge soaked in vinegar over the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if it discovers the marrow fully; then put in a sponge of sponges, and then sew from one part to the other the corruption, and be sure to sew for the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint and sew the bone or that which contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, if there is no other vein but that which covers; and if the corruption is at the wrist or at the ankle, if it is strong in that thing, but whatever it is, it must be enquired about that corrosion, how it opened; and it must be made manifest in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not make you do wrong; and that the incision and the sutures which cover these bones are many, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of spots, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it must appear similar to the work of this instrument; and that the work will show you the instrument of which you have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases; if you think that the instrument is that which is necessary according to this, that it must be so.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder may be dislocated by force of the hand, or by pressure of the teeth, or by the violence of an enemy. And when you have treated this corrosion with medicine, and it avails you nothing, if you cover that limb until the corrosion is gone, that the patient may escape from this death, or from the malice which is greater, the defect of the limb; and the sign of that is that the limb becomes black, as though it were burnt by fire, and afterward there follows the blackness, because that corruption of the limb spreads through the limb and takes hold of the whole body; if you are slow to cover it, and if it is by the percussion of some venomous creatures, as the scorpion of the sea and the viper and others, if the corruption is at the head of the bone, if you do not give it space to come out until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes up to the hand, if the hook is at the joint, so that the callous does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the hook is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and nothing but the quantity of its force is of use; and do all this while the callous comes or goes: if it comes at the first joint, the hook follows the other joint; and if it comes or goes, the hook takes hold of all of it; and if it comes up to the leg, if the hook is at the knee; and if it comes from below the knee, there is nothing else that can save the patient but to leave the limb exposed until death; and the mark of the hook or the thread that was left there, and extend one minister from the lower ligament and one from the upper ligament, and you remove the flesh that is between the two ligaments at one spatulate wide, until the bone is exposed; then take out the hook or thread, and put in place a bandage of lint, so that the thread does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient further damage and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows from a wound while working, if you cauterize the flesh too hastily, or put on restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and then bind the limb securely with a strong ligature; and I will tell you of a case in which a black spot appeared which seemed to burn like fire, and that corrosion began in the bone of the forearm, so that it consumed the whole limb; and when we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the limb, it became healed; and long after the corrosion had vanished, it returned again, and we had to amputate the limb.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does the postemer come loose in the marrow, and remains so long that it forms a great gathering of bones; then it breaks and tears, and in the leap of the bones, and breaks the marrow, just like vessels; and the skin which is under is just as thin as a tapestry of thread, and does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, like such diseases are called "sain," and not "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it comes down to the bone under the skin, it is called "fistula"; and the skin which is over it, if you press it, is just like a tapestry.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	Never does the postemer come loose in the marrow, and remains so long that it forms a great gathering of bones; then it breaks and tears, and in the leap of the bones, and breaks the marrow, just like vessels; and the skin which is under is just as thin as a tapestry of thread, and does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, like such diseases are called "sain," and not "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it comes down to the bone under the skin, it is called "fistula"; and the skin which is over it, if you press it, is just like a tapestry.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the arm is fractured, if you do not leave the limb to swell, and if you do not cover the wound as you see, it appears in such a way that the arm is set lower than it should be; for when the arm is fractured, if you do not leave the limb to swell and if you do not cover the wound as you see, it appears in this way: that the arm is set loosely forward, and leave nothing of the limb; and take consolidating medicines to bring out the bone, and stretch over a cloth that covers the whole limb; then bind up the force of the limb at the part where the break is most wide, because there is often swelling on the other covering according to the quantity of the break, and put the limb back on the bone to align the fracture, and do not leave the great covering until after once; and the one who comes out of the limb often causes the fracture to slip, and tears what is cracked from the fracture, whether it is poison or blood or enough, or digested or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine has reached its full extent and you see the nature of the swelling on the limb, if the swelling has already subsided, and approach the health; and then take off the bandage in the morning, or the third day, and when you take off the bandage, if you see another bandage, renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	and if it persists swollen and painful after the third day, remove the dressing and observe the wound
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes after a long tension, if you do not arouse with all your strength, because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes after a long tension, if you do not arouse with all your strength, because health is approaching. For there are some who delay their wounds by eating charcuterie in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if the belly is too full of food after a long journey, its veins do not swell; and if the veins swell too late, they are drawn out, so that if there are moist and dry medicines in substance and in effect, as in diaphinit, because there is a great part of vitriol in it, this is the last medicine. Take diaphinit and make it with rose oil and the juice of a vine equal in substance; then confirm and use. And this itself makes honey swell up, when diaphinit is not present, or take mirre, aloes and incense, crush them and sprinkle them over honey when it is taken out of the fire; and then glue it on, and extend it out of the belly, and never administer an aristologist for a long time, or celestial roots, which is as much like flour sometimes and hundredweight; and use simple or compound: crush them, make powder of them, and sprinkle them over the honey that I have mentioned, and use it. And if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then its veins swell up, and the bones are fractured, or the limbs are deformed; if the cure of the fistula is as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the incision of the abscess.</start_of_turn
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the armpit, or by chance arises in other two; and when it is neglected, if it comes to an abscess of the thumb, it contracts and swells so much that it reaches the root of the thumb, and by chance it contracts all the way; and there comes the erosion down to the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the thumb is large, and the colour is dark brown.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have treated it as we have said in the previous chapter, and the cure does not help, if you must, cut away all the superfluous tissue that remains of the thumb, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help when the bone is sound, and the thumb is healthy; but if the thumb presses on the marrow and begins to swell, and the black bile comes, if you must put off the root of the thumb that point the marrow, and bring the thumb up, and cut away this little marrow lightly and gently, and put on the remaining marrow medicines that are astringent and corrosive to burn away everything; then heal the wound until it is healed
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the bone is corroded and the swelling persists, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed; and if you see the thumb corrupted, if it swells up just as much as it has been said, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and causes great pain, it is better to remove it first; then cut off the nail at the base of the thumb, and guard that the cut does not go deeper than the pulp of the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, put something over it that will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain comes from the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two thumbs that are born on the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is part where there is bone, and never is there a nail, or anything that is born in the root of the joint, or the birth is on some of our thumbs from the nails.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without a stain does not move; he who is born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance moves; the size of him who is fleshed is slight, in part as much: size like the root of a broad spatula.
