Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint if he is grieved must cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or must afterwards without stain, if you must, first grasp the rounded flesh around the bone until the bone is set, then grasp the bone to a convenient distance from this one, and then heal until it is sound
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come as a result of these things come from birth, or from the swelling of a wound, or from the burn of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you must grasp that which is swollen, if it must be repaired in its natural form; then put between two bands or cloths soaked in rose oil, that it does not stick; or you put between two pieces of soft sponge, until it is healed, as it must be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When a swelling comes to neither of its two ends with the palm of the hand, if you manage that dislocation as it seems necessary.
des vils	Des vils.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large blood vessels covered with dark, melancholic fat, which come in greater numbers in the limbs that move and work, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is proper therefore that you do not give him any purgatives of colocynth, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire is in two ways: one is with the cautery, and it treats the black blood; the other method is that you ligate the vein, and you pull it out whole.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first, warm the affected limb until the fat is softened, without stripping it; then stretch the limb of the patient from under the hipbone to the knee; then cut the vein in one, or two, or three places, of a large size; then ligature and pull out the black blood from your hand, from the tip to the wrist, until as much as the patient can tolerate; and then ligate it, and command that he eat flesh that is fatty black; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.</start_of_turn
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The wounds of the patient are as follows: let him open the limb with the hand, if there is hair, then put or bathe it in hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, if the patient is in fire, then make him lick the fire, and then hold his hand over the vein at its long end at the elbow, or in the lower part at the ankle; then draw the leather over the nail, and loosen the vein from the heel up to the ankle; when it appears as if a white thread; then release the nail, until it is freed from the leather, then tighten the nail slightly, and hold in another place for three twoths; then loosen the leather over the vein until it appears, then return to the original position as you did before; then make another burn, or several if necessary, and when it is finished, draw out the nail and hold it in the hand, until it is fully withdrawn; and keep it still, for if it moves, it will not be possible to draw or lift it, and will cause harm to the patient; and when it is fully treated, remove the scab from the wound with wine and rose oil.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and tortuous and surrounded altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, if you must open it, do so with force, but do not close it; and take it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And if the eye is curved and tortious, and is not straight, as we have said, if you must open it, do so with force, but do not close it; and take it out as we have said before.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture; and by chance it comes out elsewhere except in the limb, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decaying leather, as when it comes from the serpent's body and towards, it is enclosed between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there are signs of the beginning of this vein swelling, that is to say, if there comes into the limb a very great inflammation, then it contracts the blood, and the vein begins to swell, just as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the vein bursts open, if you believe that you can wrap around around a piece of sponge from one and a half fingers to two and a half, and the thumb, and leave the sponge in the limb, and every time that it is about to slip away, if you wrap around the sponge with the thumb, and the thumb itself; and if it is too long, if you cut off a part, and wrap around the remainder, and do not cover it in its root, until it is all gone; for if you cover it, if it returns to the flesh, it causes swelling and pus or death, and is a bad disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and continuously until it is completely healed, and that nothing remains or remains stiff; and never is this vein well treated when it is treated with five palms of sponge, or ten, and one hundred has already come to me of this, from ten palms of length, and when you cover it, if there remains one hair or perforation, and pierce it through to the end, so that all is gone; and either evacuate the matter that is inside, and bring medicines to the limb without causing further pus, and then cure it like the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never in this vein have I seen hands remain, even when it bursts through the wrist joint or the wrist itself, and from there comes moisture of pus, and where it leaps rains; cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never in this vein have I seen hands remain, even when it bursts through the wrist joint or the wrist itself, and from there comes moisture of pus, and where it leaps rains; cure it as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often causes swelling of the calves, and is a small vein that arises between the skin and the flesh, and runs throughout the body, up and down, and is felt quite often from limb to limb, as long as it reaches the skin or moves, and leaps fiercely; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as bile, worms, blood, and carbuncles or tumors. And it is suspected to be malicious, for when it runs through the body and reaches the head, and comes out at the other end, it often returns and destroys the marrow.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not yield until it goes away: if it is certain, then bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, then press upon it and pull out, and if it does not come out, if you burn it with fire above, until it dies; and the greater damage it makes, if it turns black, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the black, strain out its hair, then press upon it, and pull out. And you must use the patient of ointment of corrosive medicines for the humors which are carried, and feed him nourishing food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not yield until it goes away: if it is certain, then bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, then press upon it and pull out, and if it does not come out, if you burn it with fire above, until it dies; and the greater damage it makes, if it turns black, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the black, strain out its hair, then press upon it, and pull out. Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and is a pain that comes in the limbs following one another; and I have seen this happen.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and found her arm swollen at the elbow; and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm. I observed that it grew as quickly as a worm on the back, more quickly than anything else, like silver when it comes out of the furnace; the pain departed from that limb and settled in the armpit, and then spread throughout the whole limb, so that it reached the other arm; and she told me that it would recur whenever she moved the limb, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered what caused such a movement of the limb against the limb, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I do not wish to say that the pain of one limb moving to another has ceased; but I do not wish to lie, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because her bones were dry and her veins were exposed, and because of that appeared that constraint; and I do not see it for any other reason, for those who have moist bones and veins restored
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the healing of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if the lymph above and below is swollen, and then press above as long as this wind-gust is confined to the limb; and cauterize the limb. And if you do not see it in your eyes, if you cure this that discharges the wind-gust, as with foul pills and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	And when you see the healing of this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if the lymph above and below is swollen, and then press above as long as this wind-gust is confined to the limb; and cauterize the limb. And if you do not see it in your eyes, if you cure this that discharges the wind-gust, as with foul pills and pills of serapin, and similar others.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	If the antidote for those who suffer from wind-sickness, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of their shapes is such that some have large points, small, hooked, and rounded; and some have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those that have pieces; and the one that bites in no limb bites in two ways: either in the principal limb that bites like the brain, the shoulder, the liver, the kidney, the spleen, the intestine, the bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the head of the shoulder dislocates, do not delay in extracting the arrow, for death often follows in its wake; and when such a bad sign appears, do not hesitate, for the arrow is not easily withdrawn, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the arrow pierces the bone of the shoulder and the scapula above the brain, and there is scraping and swelling and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of the mind, vomiting of bile; and by chance there is no movement of the nose or ears; or by chance the speech and voice are lost; and there leaps out from the wound a white moist discharge resembling pus, and in the same way as brown blood; and if this sign appears, if you hesitate, withdraw the arrow for it is not in vain.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the tooth aches or bites, it is near the left breast and feels as though it is caught in something hard, without any void; and by chance the tooth moves like a poulp, black blood spurts out, and there is cold sweat and a cold shiver, and fainting: there is doubt that the patient will survive.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seat that never lets go of its wound is that it leaps without prompting, the throat swells, the patient turns pale, and breathing is difficult.</start_of_turn

Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who had an arrow in his face, and had a deep wound; and he suffered great pain; and many others died.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take out an arrow from the king's arm, which was stuck in the flesh so that it was leaning to the right; and it had been there for three days. I went to cure her after that when it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very sore.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to treat it gently, and did not feel it; and there was no swelling or pain on the right ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I put on the plaster around the wound to digest the swelling, and the arrow came out by itself
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept it covered for a few days, and when I took the plaster away, the wound was healed, and the patient was able to move his limb without pain as long as the arrow was still inside his flesh; and he told me
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound the corrosive medicine of vinegar by hand, while it was still overspread, and held it in place, and felt the head of the splinter that was coming out at the root; then I closed the wound with the said vinegar medicine, until the head of the splinter appeared visibly; and it went away completely in two and a half months, and then it became wider so that I could remove the sutures, and I held one part and the other, and was not able to do anything; so I continued to work subtly and cunningly in various ways, until I had made the sutures as well as they should be, according to what is said at the end of this chapter, as I did, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it nevertheless, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me of the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you place your cure upon that which I do not speak, for the books do not teach me this; but you know masters better than anyone what is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, in descending order of the things that come to pass in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit from limbs or are ficxed by force, for there are two ways of handling them: either by force or by the wound; and that which leaps forth by force of the hand or enters, is an arrow that has penetrated flesh, and leaps forth never more.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it as long as the flesh is borne round, and be joyful of the issue; and just as if it were pierced in bone, and it cannot issue, if you leave it in that way for some days, and it moves slightly; and then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if it has pierced deeply through everything, as long as the flesh is swollen, and then you pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the splinter is fixed in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents which I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but leave it as it is until it is even again after some days, for if the splinter comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the splinter is fixed only in the bone alone, and does not come up to the surface, and remains in the patient for some days without any other mishap, if the pain is great, then it must be removed.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is firmly caught only in the flesh and does not reach the surface, if administered with poultices, as I have said; then cure the wound while it is still sound.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is seen in the bone and we cannot see it, if it has all its might; if you see it, if you can remove it without any instrument; if you do not see it, because of the extent of the wound and the depth of the splinter, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, if the pain is great; remove the splinter if you can. If there is an ear attached to the splinter that holds it, if the bone that is fixed by two parts of the muscle that you must remove, and then break or tear the ears of the splinter as much as you can, until you can remove it; and take care that you do not break the splinter, that you remove it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	and if you do not do it once, if the limb remains stiff, then pull it out again, for extraction is better than suffering.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If blood flows out due to the wound, do not oppose it; if it is necessary, close the incision of the vein and the belly, and take care as you would to remove an arrow, or to break a bone; or, if you are in doubt, follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it finds no passage, or if the skin is swollen in that place if it is seen or felt: then leave it alone, as long as the teeth can hold it; and then extract it: if it breaks now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held to the bone, if you round your hand around it, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then withdraw it.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be extracted, if you leave it in, and then restart the extraction until it is extracted; and if there is much blood in the wound, if there is too much, if the wound is deep, and you see that it is necessary, if there is a tool with a hook, so that the tip of the arrow enters the hook of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is hooked, if the instrument has a pointed tip entering, to relieve the extraction.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the bandage is surrounded, then it is necessary that you grasp all the fat around or the venom is, if you wish, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the bandage tears or breaks at the belly, the bladder, the ribs, or the chest, and it is close by, and you wish to cover it, if you grasp; and keep holding the abdomen and the nerves, and then extract it, and then suture the wound, if necessary; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tweezers used to grasp the clots is like the beak of an osprey, and thus be the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are various sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the clot
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the bone is like the wing of a bird, to press at the tip of the bandage, as it is like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the clamp to ease and to hold if it is thus made:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the common veins bleed easily.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins which one must know about in number XVI, that is to say: two veins which are behind the ears, which are called “herbech”; and two arteries which are in the two temples which appear; and two veins which are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called “aspires”; and the vein which is under the brow; and the vein which is at the top of the nose; and two veins which are at the collar; and two veins which are under the armpits, which are called “augeherich”; and two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins in both arms are five in number: one is the cephalic, which is on the left side of the chest; it is called the 'chief vein'. The second is called 'fast', and is composed of the cephalic and brachial veins; it is called the 'arm vein'. The third is either the right or left costal vein; it is called the 'belly vein' and lies above the rib cage. This is the one which is most frequently seen on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar vein is between the elbow and wrist; if there are two, there are also two in the leg and foot: one is below the bony prominence of the left costal arch, the second is the popliteal which is at the ankle of the right side; the third is called the 'radial', which is in the ankle of the left side. There are three veins in the other leg, below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of veins that are behind the ears helps to expel old blood clots and foreign matter; and the quality of the blood, as I have said, is that you raise the head of the patient and wipe the blood or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient’s neck with a clamp, until two veins appear behind the ears in two loops depending on the head: if the patient has a dark spot there, then take the lancet and pierce the vein up to the bone, then hold the hand over the whole vein, and cut and the vein well two must go through, and make the blood spurt out until you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries which are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient pilgrimage, and soda, and obtalmia customarily used, and at the root of the tears there are pus; and the quality of the physician is such as I have said: and that the patient strains his neck, so that the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse down to his thumb, and then he seizes the edge; then he lays his hand over the vein at the top of his thumb, and pulls out the lancet, and lays the vein at the top, and the skin, as he has done in two other veins, and makes the blood flow according to his necessity; then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on a bandage; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in the book concerning its treatment and extraction, or its beginning.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the vein in front is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein, for there are diseases of the face of ancient times, and migraine, and redness; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck twisting, as much as the vein bursts; then take the instrument which is called "burr," of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein; for there are diseases of the face of ancient times, and migraine, and redness. The quality is that the patient strains his neck twisting, as much as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument which is called the "burr," and put its point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or something else, and let blood flow as much as you see fit; then release the patient's neck and ligate the vein until it is whole and never more bleed with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper for me to tell you that the flames must be too great; and the same throughout, for the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are two fingers wide is useful for the swelling, and the tension, and the redness, and the yellowing of the oil, and there are diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is that the patient strains his neck twisting without any reason, as before; then do the same, and either let the blood clot, or leave it for a long time with a wide flame, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fickle, by chance if it breaks; then make a drain of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up, and hold it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	When the blood of the vein does not flow as it should, and is clotted, and has diseases of the face, as with migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old; and when the quality of the blood is that the patient stretches his neck, then grasp his hand with your left hand, take the burning flame and hold it long in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open very well indeed; do not push too much, but correct the blood as you need, and then leave it for the night, for it is much better restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	When the blood of the two veins helps to ease the swelling, and to begin the mixing of humours, and to remove diseases, and to stop itching, and to dissolve corrodens, and herpes, and worms; and the quality of the blood is that the patient stretches his neck both front and back, as we have said; then let the master sit above the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat, then open the vein widely for a long time, and take out the blood gently, or as much as seems necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then close the vessel, and gently tighten the veins in the middle, so that the patient is not stifled; and leave it like that until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	From the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper limbs helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	From the blood of the veins, if you are to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said; then open the vein, and behold two veins, one on the right side of the vein and the other on the left side, and know them by this that they are black, and that they have small black veins around them: consequently close one and the other, for if you do not know them and you are in doubt, if you close the greater part of the armpit, and the two veins that are below and above, this is a foolish method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the blood below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins below the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and this is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and stretches out the tongue, and looks under each rib towards a black vein: close both of them, and do not poke too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins that commonly bleed profusely are commonly healed in two ways: either by pinching with a great flame that is broad like a mirror, or by means of an olive oil so long as it runs in deep cuts, and this is called 'anesil'; and they are broad and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is often mentioned as a mirror, and is wide as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is a master who can open large veins filled with visible blood, which contain much blood and blood clots; and this is the form of the olive oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle to burn at the point, and it is for the health of the veins that are subtle, or there is subtle blood that has clotted.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to cure diseases such as sore throat, cough, pain in the chest, and pain in the belly; and it is useful for the well-being that it flows smoothly, and that it stops the artery that is below.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he grasps the toe, and blood flows, if the wound is closed as I have said; and let the flame not be lingering, but severed like an aspen.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the pulse does not clearly reappear, if you must extract it, and bind another; or you wish no further bleeding, or you prefer to leave the vein open instead of the arm: it will reappear clearly; and grasp the flame as an aspen, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the blood vessel burst, if you must now extract the arm, touch the vessel until you know the pulse; then sign the wound, and then bind the arm, and grasp the vein with the flame as an aspen; and beware not to cut the artery when you see the vessel swell, for that is the artery: stop it immediately.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurt out like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor frothy, suspect that it is without an artery: haste then, and put your thumb on its length, then bind your thumb if it does not bleed; many times it has happened to me. If the wound is bad, leave it alone and do not move the patient; be on guard and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is without stain, and thou feel pain, and the physician is not present, if the vein should burst, for the head of the shoulder retires itself; hold it still without stain.</start_of_turn
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bandage of physician’s rosin, and make a loop of it, and take hold of one end and bind it well up to the other; if it does not bleed, that is good; if not, if the physician has said, powders that stop bleeding; the bleeding will not be great in many positions by the small extent of the wound, and the position of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein is in the middle so that it treats the blood clot from the head downwards, and from the ribs outwards, because it is composed of the balsamic and cephalic humors, as we have said; and it is necessary for the patient to be aware of the nerve that is outwards, and if it is not too deep, and he finds the nerve, he swells it and the blood is either clotted, and by chance cannot be healed; and this nerve is often opened, and if it is not opened in some people because of its subtlety, it is necessary to take the blood from the instrument that numbs.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if the wound is deep.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein is of great aid, that it pulls blood from the head downwards, and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to cauterize with the olive or myrtle flame, because this is the safest of all veins, because it has neither bone nor nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Whatever be the case, it is best to request the most gentle handling at the first time, and grieve nothing if it does not succeed; and by chance it may be successful in some cases where it did not succeed the first time, but grieve nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of blood is as you think.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that blood should only be drawn for two reasons: to preserve health and to ward off future illnesses; and it should be drawn from one of the three veins that are either close to the surface or deep: namely, the cephalic, facial, or basilar; and it should be done immediately before prayer and fasting, and after meals when the signs of fullness appear; and it should be drawn at the beginning or after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Blood drawn for diseases has no definite period, but whenever necessary for a pulse or nut, at all hours and in all conditions; and it is not permissible to draw blood from children until they are twelve years old, or from women for more than four months up until puberty
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not remain alive who have passed .lx. years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone feels well, in whatever way, if he defends the intestines from a lesser fistula, if he has teeth clenched tightly, so that the veins do not draw out intestines with the superfluous humors that are nourished by these principal members; do not let him eat too much meat or drink, or vinegar; and if he vomits after eating, or has a swollen belly, and many pains, and sleeplessness, and loss of appetite, and vomiting, and a sore belly, and many women’s works, and trouble, and anxiety, and all the works of virtue, or by some weapon or poison; then secretly restore the humors, if they are not too great, by food, drink, and medicine, if you can; then enter or bathe, if nothing else hinders you, to secretly restore blood and keep it within the third part [of the body], as we have said; and keep him occupied with work, with drinking, and with luxury, and similar things; and keep him bound and joyous, and let the patient be higher than he was before, and wipe his hand twice or thrice, and then remove the ligature cautiously, for if it is too tight or loose, you will not be able to correct it without; then wipe the body with the hands, until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the patient with a little oil, then put his hand of his left hand on that vein below the elbow, and keep it there until the vein returns to its normal state.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For some veins, when they are inflamed like strings, if they are filled with windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if it opens the vein, the wound is too wide, because of this one must advise the physician of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If he grasps the vein too tightly, if the wound is too wide, for this reason it is necessary that the attendants be informed of these matters. And if he grasps it too tightly for the first time, that is good; but if this does not suffice, he must begin again, slightly loosening the grasp or the patient will faint.</start_of_turn>
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the limb is swollen and the patient becomes restless, and he leaves one or two fingers open, and does not bind the arm: by chance there will be abscesses afterwards; do not enter or bathe, but restart the bleeding when it stops; and if it is a small wound, or if it lacks a visible cause and you doubt that there is as much blood as you see, if you have confidence in that wound itself with all the flame directly; and do the work skillfully, even if the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not immediately start to draw out the blood, put on a piece of lint soaked in oil, because it softens the flesh of the blood; and it makes the blood clot in this limb the oil that is on it. And give the oil-soaked lint in gulps so that you stop the flow of blood; and this itself brings about a tingling and swelling of the parts when it is put on the limb. If it is too subtle, it will escape when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess which happens many times, even though it is not painful except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are in a hurry, put on the limb a wet sponge and a little oil, and hold for an hour; and it is to be known that you must do this after the bloodletting of the vein, and if it remains in the limb after some days no blackening or greening shall occur if you do not make it so; and if you see it, do not put anything of aloes or myrrh mixed with mustard, honey, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is abscess and appearance to the blood of the basilisk: put your hand there, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.</start_of_turn
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Except that you do not put anything of what we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but you must do indeed plaster dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it be until it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it is subtle; and if it is too thick, leave it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for the one who is firm and strong, and who has the mastery of extraction of blood, to make the wound larger; and let the flames be large. And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and keep it healthy often, and must keep it healthy by cutting across, not by pricking. This method of bleeding is safe from the damage of blood and nerves, and is worth more than bleeding for a long time without making it wider.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one who has a cold complexion, it is fitting to give soft bread soaked in the juice of green pomegranates; if he is exhausted, if he has lost blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, let him mix in front of the bleeding soft bread soaked in mustard or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he has pricked himself with blood, after the evacuation of moisture, then it is certain that he will vomit bile, and a fragrant vapor, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees it is going to vomit again, and is well another time, if it is caused by great bleeding, he must rest and lie still, as much as he can
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits after the first bleeding and has a strong pulse, if he rests for nine hours after the first bleeding or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who is well otherwise, if he must be well in two days or three
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which is already swollen, and causes fever; if it is necessary to drain a great quantity, and expand the opening as much as it cries out; then that all the blood should be restored, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not come again in place of the vomit, and this often happens; and it is not right that you should see it slip from the arm, and make the vomit blood for the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, extend the arm fully, for that would be bad; but leave it as it is until it has vomited the second time; or you point at the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein has vomited all the blood, and put some wool on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it and do not restrain it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, it is good to drain blood a second time, if the same is in the same limb, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The blood in the arm is pale in comparison to the vein of the shoulder because it is composed of it.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	If the patient’s hand is immersed in hot water until the pulse is red; then bind it moderately so that the wound opens well; then pass the needle through, neither too large nor too long; or make a large perforation and draw out the blood well close to the wrist joint; if this does not suffice, immerse the hand again in the hot water and leave the blood to clot in the wound until sufficient; and if this is the case, do not withdraw the hand from the hot water, for more blood will be shed in this way than in the case itself; and the blood of this vein is more valuable than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver; the method is: strain the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein escapes if it is seen; and if the needle passes through, and if you press it in all, if it does not bleed; do not press too hard, for the nerves are already quite bare of flesh; then immerse the hand in the hot water once more, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not attempt to extract it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as well as you can, if you put oil on the vein or abscess and keep it warm, and do for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said before concerning the right side.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the spleen is worth for all the diseases which are in the chest, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, diseases of the rains, and of the uterus and the ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And its quality is such that when the patient has a hot fever, and sweats on the chest so that it becomes wet, and lies down at the joint of the bone; and the chest is at the ankle, and from there the bone goes out with rains; as much as a small or large rain, or at the ankle, that much is worth
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you wash the wound on the limb, if you take care of the nerves which are outside, and if you move the limb as if you were combing; and let the flame go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved, if you reset the limb in the water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient must be bled for the first time, if it starts again at the second time from under a little space, because the blood is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the same with the spleen of the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that has clotted.</start_of_turn
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient enters or bathes in blood, it is strained from under the ankle twice by twisting, for otherwise it will not open the vein; and if it opens, let him do so in all the ways that you can, and through and through; and it is better that you cover it, for the wound is deep, and it is likely to close with hands alone.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find that the blood has opened or drained out, and if there is little or no pain, and if there is swelling; do as much as you can to stop the bleeding, and then bind up the wound, and put on a bandage; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horn, or cobwebs, or glass; and are applied according to two methods: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this bloodletting which is done by cutting has two methods: either it is done with great heat, or with cold; and bloodletting which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done in twelve pulses, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the nape of the neck; and two on the two costal cartilages; and the sponge is placed under the chin; and two sponges under the scapulae; and a sponge on the buttocks; and two sponges under the arms; and two sponges under the legs; and two sponges under the ankles; and bloodletting does not treat any illness except for superficial veins that are scattered throughout the body, and for this reason it does not cause much pain, as when we do bloodletting of a vein; and it is not recommended except when it is administered, neither with great heat nor with cold, in any disease that comes from repletion, as long as all the swellings are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if need be of illness compels it, or by custom, if the physician has seen a woman menstruating for a whole month at the beginning or at the end, and every month in between; for there are some who, when they must vomit, have a heavy head; and there are some who find swelling and redness in their face, in their head, and at the throat, and dark circles under their eyes; and there are some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, have lost their tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who think, and see nothing but blood and fear and death and other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when moisture is in the air, we command them to wait for two hours before they can go outside.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the womb helps to ease the pain of the head … which comes from these dark circles under the eyes; and it does not suffice for me that this vomiting should be after the evacuation of all the humours; for this vomiting is in place of the blood of the head, and it does not suffice for me save those who are of cold complexion in use, or who have a headache, for this makes them suffer much discomfort; and for this reason I do not advise vomiting in these uses except for those who have neither cold fevers nor other diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is sick in temperament, if he becomes unconscious, and for this reason it must be placed a little lower by the doubt of unconsciousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.
