The wind blowing in the neck is in lieu of the blood of the head and the bile, and for this reason it is worth at the least the stretching of the jaw, the fracture of the channel of the tonsils, and all, and even swelling; and it is to be feared, because if it stays too tightly, it can cause stiffness or swelling of the belly or the chest or the groin.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind that is in the collar is worth as much as the pains of the head, and pain of the brain, and swelling, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in lieu of the blood of the bile; and it is to be commanded to the patient that he express his hand to put it in, that he does not compress the artery, and does not leave discharge of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow low over the mouth, and at the corruption of the gums, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the power of the healing of the twelve leaves.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind of the shoulders is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to tighten too much, because the flesh is delicate, and knows nerves and arteries
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth as many bruises at the foundation, and as diseases of bones, and it is known that the swelling should be great, and of a coarse texture, that it must be thoroughly treated; and by chance, if it should happen to be superficial, if it breaks, it will cause great wounds.</start_of_turn>
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs swell widely open, because they draw blood from all parts of the body, and cause old wounds of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and reduce the flowers; and are in place of the upper jowls, and of the calves, and all of them cause the body to swell afterwards along its length, and cause vomiting in various conditions.</start_of_turn
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	When the vacuum is placed first thing empty, and then with moderate warmth, put it on the patient immediately, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see a little redness of the flesh and blood; then stop, and remove the vacuum, and take care of the body, for there are many who have suffered with this, and clear pores: if you do but wound once only, you will make large wounds and deep incisions; do it gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not too large, if you must wound it, do so but once: the first time to staunch the flow of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must wound it, do so but three times; and when our wings draw blood from the wound, if we are only slightly wounded once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed profusely, we must repeat the incisions often; and if the bleeding does not cease, if it is fierce and abundant, we must know when to stop, for if the wound is too deep or the skin is tough and has many pores, we must apply an aperitif and dissolvent ointment to the wound: such as violet oil, sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; or if it is in summer, cresson oil, or lily oil, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If excessive sweating is great and cold, take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of angelica, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If the wound has a tendency to suppurate and has large pores, oil should not be used, but rather the wound should be washed with rose water, cold water, or vinegar, or cucumber juice, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if anyone has a moist mouth, if he gets up easily, or from mistletoe, and sumac, and the like things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive humours rise from wine strong, or from seawater, or from decoction of rue or chamomile, or from other things of the like; and they must not fear to use the ventouse beforehand the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventosation, and must know that he must rise when he should rise and when he is risen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware those who are sickly are cold and fiery, and if they are too hot and inflamed; if you must take things cold, such as grapes and cucumbers and lettuce at ease, and other things of the like; and eat mucilage, and barley broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if you take honey syrup and fragrant wine moderate, which is between strong and new, and eat porridge, and eat mucilage, and small oils and barley; and when he should drink, he must drink more than he should eat; and must give to others no food of triacle or mustard before or after the ventosation, for to comfort the principal members; and be discreet about it, but do not let him drink anything else.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and the kidney, and upon the belly and the buttock and the groin and the heel, for in these members there is no suffering from wounds save for the extraction of blood from one member to another; for as we put on the thumbs when we do not want to bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb; as we put on packs upon the belly and the buttock to soften the limb; and to stop the pain, when there is swelling or a fracture, for by its attractive virtue it attracts the swelling, or evacuates the fracture from its place; and thus it makes elevation when put upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind, and these packs are administered empty save for so little as to slightly suctor; and never are they administered together with fire, and never are they administered full of hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the pack with hot water or with water in which there are herbs that are conducive to this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two broad palms and half of a palm of mustard seeds, or cost the joint a thousand little holes, as when driving out an arrow; and it may be from barley or chaff before if it does not bleed the patient when putting it on the limb; and in the middle there is a thorn of barley or iron, to put a bandage in place, and these are great and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the blisters of the patients are different from ordinary things, and lean rather towards fat than towards leanness.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must put this bandage on the limb: grasp the bandage with the thumb or index finger, and pass it through the thorn which is already in the bandage, so that it clasps either at the end of the bandage or does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and there must be either above the hole we have mentioned or below it, so that when we see that it is going well, if there is any vapor, we will take off the bandage; and grasp the bandage as before, and repeat this often, if you are in doubt.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case where the disease of pleuresin is acute, having neither swelling nor perforation, it is only administered when it is surrounded by water; and it is placed only on the limb concerned. This is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	No other venoms are administered except in limbs where it is not possible to place a bandage due to their small size, such as levres and gums, and the like; and in those devoid of hair, such as nails or teeth, and others like these. And if you find veins that are soft and smooth without any sign of perforation, take hold of them; and put on a little water until they are full, but without anything in the belly; then either drain the vein and the bandage, or wipe the limb until it is red, and put on the vein again. When they are full and swollen, if it is possible to put on a bandage, put it on for this is worth doing afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this does not suffice, if you lift the limb easily, then immediately afterwards with some water, rinse well, and then dry; if the limb remains too long in the water, immerse it in cold water, and place upon it, until the swelling subsides; if the swelling is multiplied, place upon it broken glass or rags, and similar things, until it subsides; or you extract half of the hairs from the head, and leave them until they burn out naturally, if you have finished now; if you still have more to do, take other hairs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the swelling does not subside, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you insert a needle into it until the swelling subsides, and then place upon it, and as long as it feels the blood, if it subsides; and when you see that they are itching, if you sprinkle upon them a little aloes and bruised saffron, or ash, they will soon cease to itch now
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.</start_of_turn>
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, dear son, for in this chapter the learned physician reveals a thing that no ancient book or letter hath ever recorded; and for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never learned of it. I know of it only through the learning of the ancient books or through the study of it and through experience, and by the custom of my life. And I have set it down in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and have made clear the forms of the instruments which are attendant, just as I have done in the two chapters preceding.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters or the sayings which put understanding into it, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proven to be learned may learn this noble art and learn it from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twist or fracture occurs, if you must hasten the healing of the patient from one side to the other, if nothing else hinders him, if he is weak in body, or is a child, or an old man; or if his tension is not very strong, or too cold; and mix cold baths, that is to say cold showers, and oil and vinegar, and do not drink wine, do not eat fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins of blood, until you are certain that the patient has recovered from the postoperative heat, or from the swelling of the limb.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the fractured bone begins to heal, if you must order the patient to eat meat which causes great swelling, or if it has viscosity, as with wheat flour in water, and rye, and testicles, and spleen, and pancreas, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part of nourishment, muscle and bone grow more brittle.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones that break from marrow cavities do not mend well nor reunite according to their nature because of the drying up of the members; and thus also those that are too brittle, as in the bones of small intestines; but there is no cure, except to leave the broken bone alone and unite the limb together, as it is; and do not move it in any way, for this is what is recommended in such cases.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And it is observed that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the arm, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a nail to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And sometimes there is its own remedy and its own instrument in the restoration, according to what is remembered to come to its aid; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is recognized by its twist, and opens well by force, and some by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or tear, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know how to move the limb, but put on medicines that will come later, and then strain it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the nails that break off that go into the marrow, and are two parts of the joint, it now coves them to put them in place equally, even as after-stitches remain; and if after-stitches come loose, if you leave no trace, until the after-stitches are appeased; then put them in place equally with the muscle, as you must weigh them gently and cautiously, and nails that restore the limb are lighter than those that remove parts; then strain, as it coves afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if it is two parts, if it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or an arm and a hand; put the limb in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the limb are loosened, if you restore by any means the pieces to their place on the muscle that you must weigh, and keep that in your work does not cause any lesion or pain to the patient; and adjust the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think that it is not well: if the wound is healing well, and it is not strained too much, do not press as those who do who make it come by their work to swelling and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is fixed in place, if the patient is very sick and does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither while turning nor in any other way; and keep the limb so securely that he feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, if he is not at a loss, it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain; and keep him straight, so that there is no twisting when he is restored; and the quality of the limb that has been broken is in accordance with what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of a broken limb is diverse in small and large pieces and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as the bones of the arms and legs, and similar; if you can cover them with soft and fine linen; and for those that are large, such as the bones of the thighs and calves: if you can cover them with a wide and strong linen, because the large linens embrace the whole great limb and strain it equally, so that there is no swelling; then you must make gentle rotations, three times or four, according to the limb, and strain your hand one pace to the whole limb, then go down to the break and strain less, than the break then lets go a pace of the break; and soften the linen around the break and around, as much as you take a large part of the limb remaining, then take another linen and turn the rotation back over the limb break; then put back to the lower part of the break, and strain moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we have said at the first hour above; then put between the rotations linen or cloth, so that they are all even, and then tie all around with a bandage, and then put your stitches in place, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is swelling or abscess, put upon something calming the abscess burn, and which softens the swelling, and leave it in place for several days; then strain upon your toes, and let them be half of a broad cane resting firmly, or of staff from which we make nails, or of barley, and let them be as this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the cane which one puts upon the fracture be greater and broader than the others; and be as long as it is convenient for the limb in small or large; then strain upon the toes in the same way as before, and bind with a thread that is neither too thick nor too thin, and of linen wool; for if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their threads of linen string, it is a great mistake, for the thread will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will not hold well.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the blows of the stones after the stretching of their bones, if you put sponges of linen or coarse cloth on them, they will not swell up.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I shall speak of the cure for that later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And the threads that he cannot bear to hold are those which break first of all.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it is not permitted to set it except after five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the wound; and when this is done, the manner of the ancient plasters is used to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion. Take wheat flour that remains on the walls of a mill, and mix it with eggs, and make this confection, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common manner of plastering that restores fracture at various positions, and the same is used for women and small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed, mugwort, asafoetida, gum arabic, and mastic, in all; myrrh and aloes, in two; aloe vera, in seven; and grind them together, and mix them with egg white; for if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones very quickly, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is useful for torsion: take mugwort and vinegar, each ten; mirbane and aloes, each seven and a half; acaice, six and a half; and aromatic bile, ten. Grind them well and mix with water or eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones that have dislocated, relieve pain that arises, and reduce swelling of the bone, and bruising: take new linen, moisten it in oil and place it over the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These methods do not restore them immediately, but they are good for calming the pain and swelling.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other method of displacement that restores fractured bones: take dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial pellwort leaves, and grind together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones and for diminishing the remaining pain.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of chamomile, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, barley flour, marigold one part; grind them and mix with wine, if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar or water, and apply it.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoration are more forceful than the first, when an abscess hardens at the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of mastic, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and confect with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for some fat and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two and not too soft or too hard
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen recommends putting something dry and warm on the broken limb, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poppy seeds, and mustard, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has his bone moved from its place; if not, loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen and oste the displacement immediately; and take a light bandage, and a wet sponge, and plunge into water, and lift up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moisten with water or rose oil, and bind on a nut, until you are certain that the abscess has vanished. Leave the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be ossified, then repeat the treatment, and do not strain it so much as before; and do it cautiously until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around a bone, and if there is a recurrence, you must repeat the procedure as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the limb anything of what we have said, if you must loosen it only after three days or four, or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what we see, until the swelling has gone down and the joint has settled; then you must tighten the restraint more than before, and swell the limb, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, that the wounds will not be able to come; then you must apply warm water to the limb every time you loosen it, and this every quarter hour, and cut a little mark on the hour; by this means you will shorten the swelling in the limb and restore the limb to its proper position. That is bad, and if the case is urgent, I do not see anything better than to leave it alone and treat it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture.</start_of_turn
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are seen, and various figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone fractured throughout, from the head to the socket which is the seat of the bone, as in the case of a break or fracture; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or if the spear pierces the bone in a reverse direction, it is called this kind of fracture 'absolute'; and there are wounds of these two kinds, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or collar of bone, or fracture of bone on bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and is this wound, or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has healed in the bone is as slight as a nail, and if the fracture is small, this kind of fracture is called a «capillaire»; and if the wound is made by a wound of stone, or by thorn, or by something similar, and if the piece of bone below enters the cavity, and if the marrow is split as when boiling over a cauldron; if between the teeth of the bone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this often happens under those who have soft bones, as in children; and it happens in all these ways that small pieces break off and loosen, like stars; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus in all these ways of fracture, small pieces are detached from them as with stars, and the tension on the tense parts, and the corrupt matter that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessel is known by this that when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe grease over it, if the black fracture is opened
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no other mishap, as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes turning yellow and red, and other similar things in various situations, if you cannot otherwise make sense of it.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an imminent accident, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes first to you, and that is in the armpit, if so, it is best to remove the bone from the fourth space above the muscle as you do.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you hurry to remove the bone from the seventh space above the bone, so that the marrow of the bone is corrupted, comes the accident that we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a break of the bone comes up to the skin that covers the brain, if you must cut through the torn flesh: take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the figure of the wound more severely than you can; and if blood spurts out when uncovering the bone, or if pus comes out, do this with what is useful, and fill the cavity with wet cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the abscesses have subsided, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then when the bone is rotated to its proper position, this is done in two ways: one way if the cut is narrow in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another incision which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have many different sizes of boils, some are soft and some are hard, and are pointed, and of iron inde; and in a slight wound, do not lance the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is firm and hard, if you must pierce through, do not make holes except where the bone actually breaks through; and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not leave the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that the flesh comes out in place of the thickness of the bone, if you have holes throughout the test; and this is the form of the two methods of holes.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the bone is that you put in a tarer on the bone, and twist your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the tarer back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisions of the space between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have moved the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pins or tweezers; and keep your hand away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	When you have grasped the bone and treated it, if it is possible, hold the socket that is detached from the bone with all other instruments resembling a chisel, but make sure it is more tense and slender than the other chisels; and if nothing of the small bones remains, do not remove any scales, even if they rest upon the bones lightly. Then close the wound with sutures and dressings as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is like that of the Galenicians, which is more reliable; and the lord is very strong, and that is his word.</start_of_turn
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is proper first that you uncover a portion of the bone, either the fracture or break open muscle, so that when you have uncovered that portion, you must place the index finger of your left hand over the pointed end of this incisor lens, as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut too deeply from one side, for the part that is hanging in two costs, if the cutting is towards the bone; then hold with a small mallet above, so that you can grasp the bone lightly, and be careful of the surrounding tissue; for if it is close to the bone, if the bone is slightly displaced, because we must hold it firmly in its place, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks without piercing the skin, cut the bone as little as possible; there are small pieces remaining. If it is possible to rejoin them, do so with the blunt end of a scraper, using various quantities as needed, to fill each cavity adequately according to the work and the nature of the fracture.

En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In small cuts of other sizes and breaks that are subtle, it is prudent to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not mentioned in this art by anyone who has put their study into this area.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the socket is discovered, take a drape of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in oil rose; then place it on the wound. Take another drape doubled in two or three, soak it in wine and oil rose, and place it on the first drape. Do this more gently than you think, that you do not damage the socket. Then administer from above another linen, and do not bind more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound alone; and leave it in place for one or two days until the swelling subsides. Then remove it and administer medicines such as herbs, flour of times, incense powder, and an apothecary, and similar things; mix these things together and put them on the wound, and administer appropriate medicines in moderation. Keep the wound clean, do not leave it bloody, do not leave it gathered together, for when it is gathered together on the soft parts of the head, if it swells and becomes loose, it causes great harm to the patient. For when anything biting is put on the socket, if it is not held in place from above.

Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige. de la forcele	forcefully
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful fracture occurs many times before, behind the shoulder, and the fracture is according to two methods: when it is broken and desevree in three parts, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or if there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is towards the wound, you must have two assistants, one of whom will hold the limb that feels the forceful fracture; and the other will extend the collar towards the part; then put the fracture back in place, so that it forms as it should, and there is no sign or swelling.</start_of_turn>

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit. de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored within .xxviij. days, and in fewer than most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this treatment for burns that are fresh and new, if they have not begun to fester.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the one between the shoulder blade and the ball of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it must be restored in one of two ways: which is to take a fistful of myrrh, as follows:

And as two fingers are bent, two thumbs are bent, and hold the patient above a seat; then grasp the limb with the fist, until it reaches the armpit, and put in the middle of the fist a corb of the fist, then put on no weight or the attendants extend downwards; then put the joint back in its place, as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.
