Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs symmetrically; and it is when the fracture is fixed to the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the bone, if one of the ligaments surrounding the ankle is ruptured, and the other is stretched by the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If also it is close to the knee, and then either the ligament above the knee is ruptured, or the lower ligament; then put the hand on the bone, equal to its natural figure, and then apply the dressing, and bind it, since the swelling will not come.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is swelling above the wound, if you leave it quiet and return to your work and your cure, the ligation is made hastily.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a strong bandage doubled in two or three places, and to drain the excess fluid, then bend the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the bone and the limb below the knee, from the knee downwards; and draw the thread tight above the limb and above the bone, then put on the dressing, and put a pin on the bone of the limb; then put in the wound eight threads between the limb and the bone of silk cloth to make the pressure equal, and as you go up the fracture, and less the strain; and leave in place two threads that you had put between the limb and the bone, and put on three pins that are above, then cover again at the bottom with the thread, until you reach the end; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it be, then do not put on any dressing or swelling or anything similar.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is swelling above the wound, if it comes loose, and you address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them, if possible; and if that is not possible, it is necessary to cut the limb open, and drain the pus. Treat the wound as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case where it is set with pins, as in the arm or leg; nevertheless, in the restoration done in this way, I do not feel any pain in the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the swelling that remains in the bone after it has been restored, lasts for one or two days, or less or more, according to the variations of complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin region.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hairs that in the groin are long, break suddenly, but they fall often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If they break, if it is not just a split, or an opening, and there is pain all around, and sensation of pain, and this feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if restoration is to be made, set the round things that are round back to their place until they are properly assembled; then put on the dressing and put on a round splint, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the arrangements that we have said above in other cases, as in the case of an abscess or other similar things; and if you put in each mishap what it should have, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if restoration is to be made, set the round things that are round back to their place until they are properly assembled; then put on the dressing and put on a round splint, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the arrangements that we have said above in other cases, as in the case of an abscess or other similar things; and if you put in each mishap what it should have, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hairs that in the leg have two bones, of which one is called by right "muscle," and the other "foscile"; and they break all together as it comes to the arm, and because of this the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is whole like that. And if both bones are broken together, if they twist the limb throughout.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured at its root, the limb is twisted forward
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, if one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it twists.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When it is suspected that the fracture is serious, extend the limb and keep it straight; but if it breaks, it is better to leave it alone, as there are more pieces when it is extended, even if the extension is less severe.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take four strips of cloth that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the hip to the foot; then wrap around with four layers of lint around and below, and bind firmly in the middle, and to this bandage will not allow the limb to bend to the right or to the left, and that is good; and no one will administer anything more long than the limb, and if there is swelling, and it has several pieces, it is better to extend slightly and more gently; and to adjust as you are able.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones in general.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture; but in bones of marrow there is never a fracture, and two must suffice, and there is no other treatment except for numerous positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in bones of marrow, and you see these bones crushing one another, if you place the limb so that it would appear to be flying away, then put the limb on the ground, just as if it were falling, and then put the limb back in its place; then press until it returns to its original position; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put on a little stool under the belly of the limb, about an inch high, and strain the limb gradually, and when it has recovered, wrap it in bandages, and other things as you deem necessary
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is still loose, because you will find the bones either broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there be any two breaks, if you restore them as we have said must be two-handed; then put at the break a splint according to the length of the break, and make it somewhat wider; then put on the thumb that I have mentioned, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more breaks, break them, and put on over each break a splint as per their quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have said about other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the humerus bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is fractured, if it is made to sit out, then lean it towards the painful side and hold it there; then fill the limb with wool and put as much on as one can; then draw out the limb, leaving the back and front parts still; and then pull out the wool until the bone comes through, and put the limb back with the wool in place.  If the limb has bled, if the bone has been pulled out, and if it has bled, leave it alone for seven days or until the fracture has healed. If the fracture has healed, take a bladder of barley and bind it to the belly with a cord, and keep the bladder in the limb until the bladder is evacuated; the limb will then return to its normal position.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or woman is fractured, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thighbone; these fractures are not hidden from him who has put his study and his art into it, and he will understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration: therefore be attentive.</start_of_turn>
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is broken, take a goose beak and put it in the groin; then wrap it round with cloths, and leave it for two days or until it is healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be immediately set in order, if what we have said is true concerning these symptoms.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, if the vitriol has been delayed, if you have nothing else, then resume the reduction in this way at the same hour, or at the least as soon as possible, for if it is delayed, it will not be cured.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is swelling of the wound, if the fracture is not reduced until the swelling has gone down, do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will cause further harm.</start_of_turn
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone breaks suddenly, it is found outside the socket as if it had been discovered, then you must hold your hands lightly at the point of the break.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the limb extension does not appear to you in order to make them equal at your hands, if you have this instrument of iron which is about twelve or thirteen inches long, and the size is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary at the mire that it grasps three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the wound of the fracture; and whether round or square, that it does not press too much on the limb at your work, and whether it is before or behind, and large in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche" because it is known that the curved bone must be placed above the head of the visible bone; and once it has returned, it must be equal on one side as the other.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well hold the bone, if you must hold the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you are forced to apply an instrument that can cover this, such as a hook or saw, to your need; then remove that which remains embedded in the bone by scraping and removing the surrounding marrow.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the limb is restored, and the patient experiences great pain afterward, it is because the bone is not properly aligned in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then immediately apply a black wine stain to the wound, and keep it covered; do not place any cerate or other thing upon the wound while there is oil, as this will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars when the bone has been restored, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area as much as necessary, according to the extent of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the breaking; for many times this has happened to fools, and they have caused the patient to die or become lame or to suffer from an infection many times; or that the pain is milder and more painless than the other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the accident has passed, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to put on supports; but wrap tightly around the wound, instead of supports, a coarse cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days blood oozing from the wound, if you put on more support than necessary at the beginning, and you cause healing wounds, as with excessive medication and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it must be that the limb is kept in its place as much as possible, so that it can heal easily
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it is displaced again, and cannot be rejoined in its place, with slight fractures that there are small pieces of bone, because it must be thought that you wish to close the wound, and reunite all these fragments of bone that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if fistula arises in the limb, or any other form of corruption, if you can cure it, according to what is said in this chapter before
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other bones of the large limbs, if you do not treat it, for many times death comes from this; but leave it until it has healed naturally; by chance it will be cured by itself after twenty days or thirty, and then heal the wound if you wish; or if you do not wish, leave it as it is
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the beard that comes out of the beard hair.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	From the beard that comes out of the beard hair, we often see after the swelling of the wound, especially when it is near the joint, and it is helpful to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its natural work
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care that you are aware: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar others, that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stifling wine or with plenty of egg or with buttermilk; and put them on the wound, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then dislocate it, and repeat this until the nodes are bony; or you strain on a well-made piece of sponge; for the property of sponge is that it will harden all the swellings under the limb; and if the node has already hardened as much as a stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above is great, and to make the apparent superfluity disappear; or do not remove it from any wound, as long as it is bony, and cure it when it is healed
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored and the limb is weakened and limp, if there is any discomfort: sometimes this is because it was too tightly bound and was not properly loosed; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot regain its natural position; or because of many wounds; or because of too great a movement, not even in its hour; or because there is much blood in the body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient relax, and to make the limb firm, until the swelling is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him cheerful and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts the great nourishment, and the wound often bleeds profusely, until the nourishment returns to the limb; and restore it to its natural position.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the blessing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural work: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have done this in our land; this work is blamed, and great evils result, and by chance the patient; although if the nodulations and the torture are fresh, if you command that they be washed away with warm water, or with soft herbs be cooked, like leaves of chamomile, and roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and you make an application of a softening plaster, like good beeswax done, and you take the nourishment of chamomile, and confit with fat of gelly or oil of poppy seed, and apply the plaster again; or you take greasy figs, and grind them with dung of the colon, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone fractured by continuous rubbing and length of time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And do not move the limb suddenly at all times.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be held by iron, if it is covered up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	If the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be held by iron, if it is covered up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs without any apparent cause, if it is now necessary to restore its proper position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if you move it too late, if by chance you succeed in putting it back, you will have pain in the limb at the root; for this reason one must not move it while it is swollen: many times it brings vomiting and other pains; however, when it has subsided, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave it, until the swelling has gone down; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and support it lightly, and cure each limb as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the shoulder to the foot.</start_of_turn>
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jaws. For the jaws are loosened and the dislocation of both is frequent: either because they are fixed to the bone of their roots, and softened a little; or because they are loosened entirely, and hang towards the chin, and tear the saliva from the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself several times.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If it is whole and complete, if you must support it, do not grasp it; and in such a way that the servant holds the head of the patient, and look at my pockets of both hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible in the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two must be loosened, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften his mandible and move it in all directions
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the eye must be kept level, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they are swollen with hot water and oil, so that they are kept lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned equally, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with a soft closure, put on moist cloths in layers made of rose oil and wax, then bind them loosely with linen threads; and let the patient rest on his back, and his arms be at rest between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor attempt to open his mouth, but take moderate food, until the pain is gone and the jaw is well healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaw bones do not manage to return to their place at once, and are not firmly secured at their roots, if in comes fever and customary sickness, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove pain from the root of the tooth, and is valueless whenever it is applied with force, and it is well known.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	If the patient lies still on his back and extends his arms; then press the limb towards the breast, and it will return; then place the bandage and bind it, and strain it; the limb which is towards the breast cannot be dislocated; if this does not happen, and if it should slip even once, if you must, reset the limb, as we have said; then place the bandage and bind it, and strain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way bring back the displaced bone, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hairs that have escaped the armpit are loosened for only three methods: first, that they escape at the part of the armpit downwards; and the second, at the part of the thumb; and by chance they escape at the part above, and this is enough; and do not loosen them further by the armpit, and do not loosen them further downwards by the nerves; and many times loosen them downwards towards the armpit, even among those who have little hair, for at these leaps they will become ill; among those who have enough hair, they leap with points and return with points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there happen to be blows or fractures, and it swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and one must take care that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary indeed. As long as you are sure; then commence the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocation is known when it is forced towards the armpit, and it makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their divergence a bulge; and at the head of the shoulder there is a pit, and the armpit touches the head of the shoulder, as if it were a nipple; and the patient cannot move their hand to its place, neither make any movement; and if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you will find it immediately on touching; and this method of dislocation is not sufficient to bring back, when it is new, or if the limb is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician grasps the painful limb high up, then places the thumbs below the armpit, and grasps the joint forcefully high up; and the physician grasps the limb and stretches it high up, because it places it below; if it comes immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said above, if you must know, the patient should be bathed in warm water; and give him mollifying and soothing medication, such as decoction of altee and fenugrec and melilote in water, or give it to him directly. Then put the patient on his back, and put under his seat a cushion of linen even, not too soft nor too hard, and put his elbow on the cushion, and keep his shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant holds his shoulder, so that it does not move backward. The shoulder will come back immediately, and if you see that it remains in place as we have said: that is to say that you make present one who is greater than the patient; and two attendants stand beside the patient, and stretch the shoulder from under the patient’s arm, and keep his arm up, so that the patient hangs down from his shoulder; and another attendant treats the patient’s hand from behind his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And we shall do the same in another way: if the head of the shoulder is loosened from the bone like a stone that is too great or too small; then let the patient lie down and have a cloth under his armpit, and let the patient’s limb hang down loosely; then extend the arm upwards from the other side and the joint will return to its place. If it does not return with all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take two thumbs and three fingers wide, which has the head of the bone that enters the socket like a nail, and press it into the socket according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the shoulder, draped with a cloth, that it does not irritate the patient, and put from behind the patient’s back; extend your arms over the shoulder of the long kind, and support the limb on the shoulder, and the arm at the wrist, then put the arm over an inch of the scapula, and extend the hands forward, or leave the forearm hanging down from the other side: the shoulder joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you put from behind the patient’s back a thumb of wool even, then put the dressing loosely of powder of wheat, with incense and alum of egg, upon the whole shoulder and around, then strain from behind the base of the thumb immediately, and turn the limb upon the dressing, and embrace the hand at its collar, and let the hands hang down alongside.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move little, until the limb is comfortable, because it will heal better; and then move more after five or six days, and turn; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is forced from its place by moisture or for another reason, if you must, administer cautery in three places as it is placed before or alongside cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and the dislocation does not heal after twenty-three days, and the limb still cannot lift the upper arm, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the dislocation will never heal in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is from front to back, and the bones, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and it is cured as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses it repeatedly, many times, until the grief is gone and returns to its first state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with a bandage, if he wishes to see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is tight, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must ensure that you reset it immediately, even if it comes loose again after you have set it; for if it comes loose again while it is healing, it will cause further pain. And by chance it will not be possible to restore it at all, even if it is at the back; in such a case it is better to leave it as it is rather than to cause further dislocation, which is more painful and can also lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it can be restored, when it is possible to restore it, extend your hand with both hands; spread your arms and hands as wide as the ruler allows, from armpit to wrist, front and back, and stabilize the joint with your thumbs together or at the root of the bone until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and grasp from the root of the bone that is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not see it return to its place, if you administer great extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder downwards, and when you have enveloped a double-length and wide bandage; and when you look at the joint with the hand, if there is any oil on the joint for lubrication, then put on the joint and it will recover; and when it is in its place, put on dry plaster with egg white, and the swelling will subside, and bend the arm to the patient’s chest, and leave it for a while, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, if you see that it does not hold firmly, repeat the manipulation of the limb and the support, and leave it thus for a few days, until it is firmly set; then you can remove the support.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, bathe and rub well, and press until it is eased; or put on the joint a sheepskin nail and leave it for a night, then take out the nail and the bone, and let him enter or bathe; when he sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the nail back in place, and enter or bathe again; do this twice or thrice until it is healed. If you see that it does not return to its place, put on a poultice of moist lint soaked in urine and bind it up; if it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is loosened, and its return is laborious, more than other joints in general; it must be immediately repositioned to its place, even if it is loosened, or if there is bleeding or swelling
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put the affected hand on a table and extend the patient, look at the hand and make sure that it rests equally on the joint; that he places his palm on the surface of the joint and stretches it until it returns naturally, you must watch to see if it is well aligned; then put the patient’s hand back on the table during extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I will look put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. If not, if the strain of the relaxed tendons calms down after the incisions, and you leave it in its original position, it will recover on its own.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you do not set it after some days, the joint will become stiff; and neither you nor the patient will be able to do anything except soften the hands, and you will not be able to extract anything, whether nerves or arteries. If there is no other remedy except to extract by cautery, do so in this case, and by chance there is nothing else.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is at rest, if you place the thumb as we have said, then strain and hold it for five days, then release and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not move well and there is no pain, if there is warm liquid [fluid], and you rub it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	... until the dislocation of the shoulder of the hand.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never are the fingers desoiled at the wrist or at the elbow; whenever it is at the back of the hand or the belly, then it is certain, and the dislocation will remain until it returns; then support the head of the finger, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for two days, and then put it back in its place; and do not touch it, as we have said, and do not move it, and bind it; do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is desoiled at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same whenever it is desoiled from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From the loosening of the shoulder bone from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder bone of the back or the neck is loosened, or there are several loosenings, if no remedy is found, for the patient dies quickly.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the urine spurts backwards, do not keep it, and many times is the limb softened, or the two thighs or two arms or one leg; and many times the spleen turns to three parts; that which turns at the back is called "gilbosite": it is cured if it is known that the gilbosite comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or impacts or similar things, they say was formerly cured by great words, but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling which comes before the heel, there is no remedy for the pain; and also that which comes directly on both sides, one cannot cure it except for that which comes from behind, as I have said; and that the patient should be stretched out on his face in one equal measure, and should have tension from his toes up to his head, that he should not bend; then put a cushion under the patient’s heel and another under the toes, and bind his ankles loosely with a bandage, and another over the heels, and over the calves, and over the thighs; and two assistants should know the bands, one at the head and the other at the toes, and be well bound, as we have said, and the patient should rest his palms on the spine until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a spoonful of three hands' length, and hold the thumb against the side; let the patient lie on his side, and put the thumb against the heel of the palm, then put the middle of the thumb on the spine; put the little finger on the other heel of the palm, and press firmly, until it returns to its place. If you see that it does not, do it at the wrist that turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If you see two tendons at the wrist of the patient of one arm, and you give them two others, and between each tendon you put a suture and a bandage, a palm's length; and in each tendon you make a hole, or the wrist is corrected, and the tendons are firmly secured. Between two tendons there is one tendon that is turning, so that the limb turns back; and there are two small tendons of a palm's length in two turns, so that the wrist returns. Then you must join the tendon which is between the bones to the wrist towards the chief, and the other tendon towards the pieces towards the other wrist, and you must bind the minister's wrist to the whole limb. The master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, if you put on a drying plaster with a lot of eggs, and then press, and then support it with a tablet of three fingers’ length, that will cause the fluid of the swelling to retreat and the part of the vertebra that is painful, and then bind it with a bandage, as we have said; and use the patient of nourishment secretly until he is well; and if nothing comes to an end of his well-being, if you must administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said above; and never give him a piece of lead, and never does it appear at the back of the shoulder blade, take care that it is not a dislocation; and it is the bone that is open, for we must not presume anything: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip joint.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and the shoulder only dislocate; it does not happen with other joints; and the hip joint is damaged in three parts: front and back, and top and bottom; the more it is damaged from front to back, and the more it is damaged from top to bottom.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of his dislocation is that when you join the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the patient’s joints than the sound, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and it is the thigh which is emptied of fat, for this is what brings about the pain in the armpit
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of such an accident is that it is contrary to the preceding ones.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this is that the limb is well placed in accordance with its completeness; however, do not double the knee excessively, for if you see that it is painful, do not attempt it at once, and retain your urine, and swell the limb, and when he walks, let it pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that one who has behind him, if he cannot expand his knee, cannot double, and is the leg more short than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is displaced from its socket.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If this semblance of dislocation persists, if it is an old dislocation and does not spontaneously regress, and there is no remedy; I do not know that there is any other remedy except for presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty in returning the joint, and stretching it inwards and outwards, and moving it to the right and left; by chance it will return, and there will be no need for any other remedy.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, if you must, appear I minister strong, and hold the limb firmly with two hands, or with one that you wish to bind upon the knee; and another minister extends his hand downwards as far as he can, as he holds his hands beside his buttocks; and he grasps it with a loop of thread upon the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend upwards and downwards together until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three instances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not happen, if you must, provide a cure for its semblance. When the dislocation is complete, if you can, support the patient above his costal cartilage, then place the limb over the root of the hip, and the limb which is beside the groin, then stretch the limb upwards towards the groin and towards the forcele; then take another minister and embrace the great limb of the painful hip, and stretch it forward: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less laborious than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not hold it firmly in this manner as we have said, if you must, bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread above the two toes and above the two knees; let the limb be extended two fingers more than the others; then suspend the limb from the top of a pole, or upon the ground two arms long; then command one minister to grasp the heel of the hip bone and let another minister accompany the patient, who graspes the hip bone, for the joint is now restored.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. And when the dislocation is before, if you must, stretch out the affected limb as much as possible, as I have said; and put the eyes on the painful part; then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the groin.</start_of_turn

And when it is completely loosened, if you make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the thigh, below the ankle; then take the thumb to your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, and extend it upwards, and hold the limb firmly; do this twice, as we have said, with both hands grasping and pulling the limb; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, make the patient lie on his back on the earth, and fix his heel firmly on the earth between his thighs, and spread his blanket around him, so that it does not bleed the patient; then hold the patient’s thigh, and another attendant extends the limb with both hands or with one hand, that it lies on the collar of the limb; then extend the thumbs equally, and hold the limb either inwards between the patient’s thighs to hold the patient when it is extended; then put the eyes equally on the dislocation with both hands, and another attendant holds the limb steady at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put on the plant of rue over a table at a quarter past nine, then the swelling forms, and you leave it for two days, and then you take it off; and you rest it until it is healed.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died: if you are not bold in your cure, if you do not know the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be ashamed; and begin with calming measures at the outset, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you rejoin the limb in its place, even as the abscesses remain; and when the limb is in its place, if you administer calming measures at the outset, cure the wound, if it is possible, with desiccated sponges; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, if the bones are displaced, do as is said in simple illnesses; and keep yourself away from fear, as I have said, for this is harmful to you according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arm and body.
